when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正要說的是 , 未來會比這還要多很多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 在1936年 , 再發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , 巴貝奇的機器是完全機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器完全是理論上的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個傢伙都來自數學的觀點 , 但圖靈告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你如何製作電腦 , 都不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論是電腦的機械裝置 , 例如babbage的技術 , 或電子產品 , 如今 , 或未來的電腦 , 或細胞 , 或 , 再一次 , 一旦我們進入奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 , 所有東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這被稱為教堂的論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage其實是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 今天我們能用電腦做所有事情 , 只有很緩慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	給你一個概念 , 它有大約1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用的是打孔卡 , 被餵進去 , 大約有一萬次會慢下zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一組小組 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以有規劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館檔案中 , 有數百張計畫和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的 , 關於分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組計畫就是我們稱之為28計劃 , 這也是我從doronswaade開始的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的運算策展人 , 也是驅使這個計劃創造出一個不同的引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有許多部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是巴貝奇的檔案掃描 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 , 第二個是研究所有這些計畫的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是模擬那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一個部分是要在科學博物館裡實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你會終於明白電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你面前有一小塊晶片 , 你得要看著這件令人驚奇的事 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 聽見它運作 。 我可能聞到它 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在那之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫了一篇文章 , 他說 , 當分析引擎出現時 , 肯定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過它 , 因為他總是對新計畫感到困惑 , 但當它打造出來時 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我要給你們一點嚐嚐一下 , 用一支影片拍攝的動作 , 影片中只是cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只不過是三組袋子 , 它會加入 。 這是加入的機械裝置 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們將會有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這場影像填寫的演說中 , 雅恩•瓦爾德將他的三項作品展示給人性 , 我們的棲息地在他的系列中 , 驚人的天體攝影像 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 他的網頁上寫著 「 六十億人 」 , 他的網站上 , 《家》 , 透過呼吸影片 , 記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅諾•阿曼•哈德在廣泛角度捕捉脆弱的地球 , 在廣度上捕捉脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對這個星球有很大的影響 , 以飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 , 這是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來到這裡 , 談論生態學 , 一年內我將二氧化碳排放為法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回家時 , 我得要殺了一個法國人嗎 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須以另一種方式來做碳排放 , 就像我每次都要做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年拍攝的最後幾張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達的沙油 , 很多污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 , 我們不想相信我們知道的事 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在阿爾伯塔人的工作中 , 有24小時 , 七個小時的時間 , 用盡可能多的油來萃取 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端 。
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙不是長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們用的石油比我們每年都多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加州的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	一百分之百的珊瑚礁可能在2050年因為全球暖化而消滅 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋生物多樣性來說 , 是非常重要的 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 , 我去年夏天拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前 , 這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在 , 大西洋和太平洋之間有一個新方法 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	從1960年起 , 北極的厚度下降了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	沒有冰 , 吉利馬扎羅有新的面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它損失了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在100年內 , 所有的山冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾說的 , 二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河上的水上 。
return of fish men .	再回到漁業男士 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類會依賴魚生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今 , 有70%的魚股被過度開發 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao的說法 , 如果我們不改變我們的捕魚系統 , 2050年 , 主要的海資源會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	美麗的圖片 , 來自非洲 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	世界上有六個人沒有足夠的食物 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多地方的主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 90%的玉米培育被用來餵食動物或做油脂 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	棕櫚樹種植園在婆羅 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每一年 , 我們都損失了五萬平方英里的森林砍伐 。

according to the u . n . , we speak about 250 million refugees in 2050 .	根據聯合國 , 我們在2050年談了2億5千萬難民 。
i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。

at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	此刻 , 我的家人非常貧窮 , 生活在深圳 , 只是為了讓自己看到我能賺更多錢 , 讓父母留下來 , 活下去 。

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟你們談談我的電影 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經四十五億年了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 已經有好幾億年了 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類已經走上了二十萬年了 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功地適應了 , 並且征服了整個星球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬種物種住在我們旁邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我親眼目睹地球和它在天空中高度的指揮者 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的幸福有關 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們仰賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	漁業 , 繁殖 , 農業仍然是世界上最重要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起的 , 遠比我們分裂的還要大 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的禮物有相同的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們仍然在養育牆壁上 , 來讓我們分開 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最大的戰役是要保護我們星球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	不到五十年的時間 , 我們已經徹底改變了它 , 遠遠超過人類的整個歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源在運作的很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們在危害自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有了解到 , 我們的速度比地球還快很多 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道今天的解決方案是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力去改變這個趨勢 , 讓它變得更好 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們在等什麼 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中richardresnick的演說中 , 基因定序會讓健康照護有多便宜又快 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷尼克:歡迎來到基因革命上 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向各位介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份關於大x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , y的複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩 , 但這只是一件小事 , 讓你變得不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的是 , 這個雙螺旋結構 , 生命的密碼是用這四個生物化學字母拼湊出來的 , 或者我們稱之為基礎 , 對吧:a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 三十億 。
is that a big number ?	這數字很大嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以把大數字丟掉 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我在這個1280年到800年的解析度螢幕上放了一個基石 , 我們需要30000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以這真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , 有y染色體的人決定將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金 , 基因組序列和出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最後一個版本被刊出了 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	全部的機器看起來都像這樣 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個基地都要花一塊錢 , 用很緩慢的方式來做這件事 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	嗯 , 各位 , 我來這裡要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以 , 現在我們用一個基因組 , 大概有50個複製體 , 我們把這些複製品切成50個基礎讀取 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將它帶入軟體中 , 然後重新組合起來 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給各位看一張圖片 , 人類基因組計畫:3gbabass , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器在其中一台:一週200gbabes 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將改變到6000年 , 這種速度的緩慢是毫無意義的 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 鹼基的價格 , 以序列為基礎 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這相當於你在1998年裝滿天然氣的車 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開木星兩次回去 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點 , 所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、古老的定序方式 , 這些都是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是木質尺度 , 通常你不會看到像這樣高的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全球定序人類基因組的能力 , 今年大約有五萬到十萬種人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道 , 基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期會有兩倍、三倍 , 或可能是四倍以上 , 未來是可預見的 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室 , 裡面有百分之二十的能力 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做北京基因組學院 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國絕對贏得了新月球的競賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她有第二階段的雌激素接收乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她被手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三種卵巢癌復原 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療治療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時 , 帶著更多的卵巢癌、更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓血癌回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸道失敗 , 八天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	所以 , 首先 , 這個女人被治療的方式 , 只要十年 , 就會看起來像血液一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	因為像我這樣的同事rickwilson , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 他決定看看這位女性後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他將皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚和癌症骨髓進行序列 , 在幾週內 , 他將兩者的基因組定序 , 沒有什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他將這兩種基因組的軟體做比較 , 他發現 , 在其他東西之中 , 是一個拘留 , 一個在三十億個鹼基的基因 , 一個叫做tp53的基因組 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種完整的突變 , 你人生中有90%的機率罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女士 , 但它的確有嚴重的、深刻的影響她家人 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有同樣的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因測驗 , 然後他們了解了 , 那麼他們就可以做定期的檢查 , 然後他們就可以在早期捕捉癌症 , 有可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦麻性麻痺症 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是個非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信這些症狀並不符合 , 透過一些英雄的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的就是反應性失調症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀的改善了 , 但他們並沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 這張照片裡的先生叫joebeery , 他很幸運能夠成為一家叫做生命科技的公司的協會 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家公司之一 , 讓這些大量的基因定序工具成為這兩家公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是把他的孩子定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 一系列突變發生在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 負責生產血清素的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在這張照片上 , 他們給這些孩子一個血清素的先驅藥 , 現在他們很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 沒有完整的基因定序永遠不會發生這種事 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前 , 成本是10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在100美金後的一年後 , 或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這樣速度就快了 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	像蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院裡 , 帶著這種延續的肚子 , 像是饑荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 餵食掉進他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百次手術之後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽 , 祈禱我 。 我在痛苦中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好在臨床遺傳學的背景中 , 他不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因序列得到吧 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 一個基因突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對於食物本質上會發生什麼事 , 會有一些免疫反應 , 這是一種自然的反應 , 造成了一些編程的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但規範下來的基因是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也說明了骨髓移植的治療 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的勞力復原之後 , 他現在吃了一口牛排 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	將基因組當成普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們眼前 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人來說 , 這房間裡的每個人 , 都能活出額外的五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這個東西 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想想地球上人類的足跡 , 以及我們能維持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來培養新種玉米、小麥、黃豆和其他的作物 , 非常包容乾旱、洪水、殺蟲 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得要繼續成長 , 吃基因改造的食物 , 這就是我今天唯一要採取的職位 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫示範他的骨髓採礦器 , 快速收集骨髓 , 讓捐贈者的痛苦減少 。 他強調骨髓的成人幹細胞 , 可以被用來治療許多終端疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟疾病 。
