and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 像是白血病、淋巴瘤 , 和其他疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛大學做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 這裡有bob , 自願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 拯救了白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何採集骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 將麻醉 , 護士 , 另外一個來自我的人 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃站在桌上 , 我們拿了這個小小的針頭 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法是 , 基本上 , 將它放到軟組織中 , 將它打入硬骨頭 , 進入突變術語 , 這是一種技術上的術語 , 且很抱負大約十種骨髓 , 每次都有針筒 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把它交給護士 。 她將它安裝成一個tin 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交給我 。 我們再做一次 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到這張手臂的尾端 , 我手上有一通電話 , 更別說鮑伯 , 他的收入看起來比較像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這種手術在40年內沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想出了一個微創的入侵方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓礦工 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式在這裡 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準視網膜病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭幾十次 , 我們只需進入骨頭 , 進入骨頭 , 進入骨盆的前面 , 或臀部的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有強力的導航器 , 上面有特殊的電線環 , 它會留在骨髓的內部 , 跟著臀部的轉動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以 , 它能讓你非常迅速地渴望 , 或吸取豐富的骨髓 , 迅速地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同樣的入口來傳遞多個訊息 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快的 , 鮑勃可以拿到一根刺激 , 當地的麻醉劑 , 把這個收割做為一種非耐用性 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小小的補助金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終 , 我們得到了兩個大型動物 , 豬研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 驚訝的是 , 我們不僅得到骨髓 , 還得到了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年僅是fda核准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是肝臟病患 。 你可以看到它遵循靈活的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人身上 , 在同一個洞內 , 會有兩條路徑 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地的麻醉 , 作為一個外在的藥品 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們再次得到 , 比同一個病人使用的標準方法要多三到六倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們的身體 , 包括骨髓內的血流幹細胞 , 這種幹細胞是一種幹細胞治療超過40年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 骨髓幹細胞被大量使用 , 來治療病人的心臟疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至神經系統治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們才剛出櫃 , 今年我們將商業化 , 棉花礦工的2.0個世代 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人簽署 , 成為潛在拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可以讓你禁止你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年紀較年輕、健康時 , 用在未來 , 你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植者 , 每年在史丹佛 , 聚集了一群人的骨髓移植者 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪葛雷特•賴西提出一個具爭議性的宇宙模型 , 可能只能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有任何問題 , 它是最美麗的8d立體模型 , 它是你從未見過的基本粒子和力量 。
physics , science , technology	物理 , 科學 , 科技 , 科技 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi在他的理論上 , 關於所有事物的理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 ! 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會盡可能地去描述粒子物理的美麗 , 不用方程式來描述 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗又不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭都有成千上萬個珊瑚礁 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些複製劑不斷地被灌輸到基因上相同的鄰居中 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們就能把個人遺漏出來 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點 , 與他的鄰居相比 , 如果那只是機會 , 命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在向我們示範把溫度變得太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題很愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是很有意義的 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤痕來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個複製劑會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯地和他一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點裡 , 體驗到他們是獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 超級聰明的珊瑚會特別準備好去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學數學準確地描述宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實不斷地分化成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	這對我們人類來說是件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗到一個可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪的現象 , 首先被薛丁格和他的貓所描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設定中 , 薛丁格在一個盒子裡 , 有一個放射性樣本 , 由量子力學定律 , 分成一個狀態 , 它被輻射出來 , 一個不存在的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在這個分支中 , 樣本放射線 , 會產生一個觸發 , 釋放出毒藥和薛丁丁格的觸發器已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個人都能獨立體驗這些現實 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	儘管如此 , 另外一個人也不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人只經歷一個獨立存在 , 而我們卻沒有看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	就好像我們每個人 , 像這裡的薛丁格 , 都是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 這是世界在微小的尺度上運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是描述可能發生的事 , 以及無法發生的事 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 所有東西都來到幾何和基本粒子的交互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只要這些交互作用是完全平衡的 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將向前描述我們如何了解這些粒子、它們是什麼 , 以及它如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 質子和反質子的光束會加速到接近光速的速度 , 並在撞擊中產生出純能量的爆發 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成一顆亞原子粒子噴射出來 , 用探測器和電腦來計算它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 位於日內瓦的cern的cern對撞機有一個十七英里的環境 , 當它在運作時 , 將五倍的電力輸入到蒙特雷市 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們不能準確地預測粒子在任何個體碰撞中會產生什麼 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都能實現 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們 , 粒子能產生什麼 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量就等於質子和反質子 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能源限制更大的粒子 , 都不會產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能源限制推到前所未有的七倍之外 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談到我們可能看到的之前 , 讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子粒子有一整個動物園 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這個房間裡 , 很多人會做一個好的生活 , 把他們推到附近 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中性伴侶 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上游的夸克有非常大的質量 , 三分之一的組合 , 使原子內部的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左邊和右邊的品種中 , 帶著相反的載荷產生抗粒子的合作夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 相同的載荷和第一代相同 , 但有較高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都和各種力量粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子 , 通過電粒子 , 與電荷相互作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫做 「 不可思議 」 , 「 弱力 」 , 只與左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克的強力作用 , 帶著一種不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 三種不同種類:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann的名字 , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有引力的力量 , 會透過它的質量和旋轉來與物質交互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 每一股力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的對應電荷進行交互作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個尚未見過的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 讓所有粒子都有質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團是我們看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看一個美麗的可能性 , 在這場演說的尾端 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 會有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	這是很多粒子用來追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	很奇怪 , 大自然會有許多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克有電荷 , 三分之一則有電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上下夸克和一個下夸克結合成質子時 , 總電荷加一加一 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 也有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩個載荷的組合:超載荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超載荷和弱荷散播到這個二度載荷空間的載荷空間中 , 電荷載荷就是這些粒子沿著垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據他們的超連結和弱荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的箭頭模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回去 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是兩者都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量 , 破壞了這個電子圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力變得非常弱 , 只要給予弱粒子一個大質量的微弱 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個巨大的希格斯粒子沿著水平的方向 , 電磁力的光子仍然是無質量的 , 與電荷在這個載荷空間的垂直方向上交互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以 , 電磁力和弱力被二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強大的力量 , 透過散播出它的兩個載荷方向 , 並在這些方向上繪製出能量粒子的載荷 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中繪製 , 並投射到像這樣的二維空間 , 這樣我們就能看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然就會把東西放在完美的平衡中 , 沿著這四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子碰撞 , 它會產生能量爆炸 , 四個載荷方向的載荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時此刻 , 任何東西都可以創造出 , 只要它擁有相同能量 , 並維持一連串的0載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的抗粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的交互作用中 , 指控總是平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐壞成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個粒子還能加入零載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些指控的模式並不只是漂亮的 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們 , 什麼樣的互動被允許發生 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強烈的交互作用 , 這種美好的六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 強大的力量粒子 , 例如這個 , 與有色的夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的夸克 , 給一個夸克 , 上面有不同顏色的顏色 , 紅色的 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強烈的互動每秒都在發生數百萬次 , 在我們身體的每個原子裡 , 把原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應到三種力量並不是故事的終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以將兩種載荷對應的重力力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入時 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個很棒的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它真的很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	此時此刻 , 這種模式符合我們目前最好的知識 , 了解大自然是如何以微小的粒子組成的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子的極限是我們能與實驗交流的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙用這些微小尺度來運作的方式非常美麗 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些新舊的想法 , 關於我們還不知道的事 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把手放在整個奇拉達上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有製造出完整宇宙的粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 在實驗達到更高的能量時 , 我們會看到新的粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個古老的概念 , 這種已知的載荷型態 , 不對稱性 , 可以從更完美的模式中產生 , 形成類似希格斯粒子如何打破電磁圖案 , 產生電磁性 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要介紹新載荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹新的方向時 , 我們會猜測沿著這個方向所載荷的粒子是什麼 , 然後我們可以將它與其他粒子旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	假如我們明智地猜測 , 我們就能在六度載荷空間中建立標準載荷 , 以七度載荷的最完美圖案為基準 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , pati和salam所提出的一個統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們觀察這個新統一的模式時 , 我們可以看到一些缺失的差距 , 粒子似乎忽略了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的運作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 包含後代的建立模式 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新勢力粒子的存在 , 這應該和弱力很相似 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在 , 我們可以在七維空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 考慮一個奇怪的事實:第二代和第三代的物質有著完全相同的載荷 , 就像第一代一樣 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二的被六個載荷所辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間中 , 他們坐在彼此的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就可以把每個粒子獨一無二的載荷給給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖形是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到第二代和第三代的物質 , 與第一代的對稱性有關 , 叫做 「 試驗 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中這個特殊的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構的一部分 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最特別的謊言團體的模式 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 彎曲的形狀有248度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個模式中 , 每個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時段 , 解釋引力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學結合在一起 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀 , 可以描述宇宙在最微小的尺度上是如何運作的 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀活在八度載荷空間的空間中 , 非常美麗 , 它總結了數千種可能的微粒之間的互動 , 每一個形狀都只是這複雜的形狀的表面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多複雜的圖案 , 都包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了一種特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間中看著這個圖案 , 沿著對稱軸線 , 同時看見所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 和任何統一的物體一樣 , 我們可以看到一些新粒子被這個圖案所需要的洞 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個落差 , 其中兩顆被派別粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們在這個模式的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是疤痕的領域 , 例如希格斯粒子 , 但它們有顏色載荷 , 和強力交互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個模式 , 給我們全e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8的圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是一個很棒的前景 , 就是這個偉大的數學美麗物品可以用最小的尺度來描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學所描述的這種想法完全不是新穎的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	在1623年 , 伽利略寫了這篇文章: 「 大自然的偉大書 , 不斷地展開我們的目光 , 寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有這些圖形 , 無法了解它的單一字 ; 沒有這些 , 其中一個在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊走 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 描述粒子物理學的數學 , 只用三角形 , 圓形和其他幾何圖形 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我實際研究這些東西時 , 數學可以組成一個暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 要確保這個數學的核心是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這種數學將我們的宇宙描述成一個生長8個珊瑚 , 粒子在各個角落相互作用 , 根據一個美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	更重要的是 , 使用像大型強子對撞機這樣的新機器 , 我們也許能看到大自然是否使用這個e8圖案 , 或另一個圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一個很棒的冒險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那就非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc發現了新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那就很有趣 , 但對這個e8理論來說 , 不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是非常危險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他類似的理論是長拍的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	許多努力都知道 , 大部分這些點子最終可能不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有很多的線條 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這個規則中 , 新的物理理論就像新創公司一樣 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就像任何大型投資一樣 , 要放棄一系列的研究 , 情緒上是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果有東西行不通 , 你就得試試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 要維持正義和達成快樂的唯一方法 , 就是保持平衡和觀點在生活中保持平衡 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡了所能 , 過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的生活 , 物理、愛 , 和衝浪我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我工作的物理成果一無所有 , 我仍然知道我已經過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	在過去的10年裡 , 我住在毛伊島上 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	這是我父母在宇宙中最偉大的謎團之一 , 我如何能一直存活下來 , 卻沒有任何與全職工作相似的就業機會 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要把你們放進那個秘密裡 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我媽ui的家庭辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景觀是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室的家 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個非常不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我花時間做我喜愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 生活著遊牧的存在很艱苦 , 但它讓我能生活在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 讓我一直很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我花了很多時間和高智能珊瑚聯絡 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白了百分之二的成果 , 但我仍然很愛它 。 所以我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的理論是所有灰色的lisi:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 這麼多人至少會感到興奮是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是要說 , 我們應該去想宇宙 , 在它的心臟裡 , 最小的事物是有可能的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 有沒有比例尺 , 以最小的尺度來看 , 還是......
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	蓋爾:嗯 , 現在我給你們看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學有關 , 已經對應到非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我所說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	而這個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 和它融入e8的圖案 , 可能是其他的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	而這些我向你們展示的點的圖案 , 其實代表著這個高維的物體的對稱性 , 會在我們所經歷的空間中被扭曲、移動、跳舞和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但像我所了解的 , 弦理論家 , 用比較小的弦來解釋電子震動 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何想像一個電子與e8有關的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	蓋爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱性之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空移動時 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動時 , 它會扭曲的方向是扭曲我們所看到的粒子 。 所以它會是:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	它更大嗎 ? 它比較小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋爾:嗯 , 據我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有可能性都在不斷地擴展 , 同時發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用珊瑚比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8進來的方式 , 就是將它當作一個與時空相連的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的 , 形狀會改變方向 , 隨著它在曲線的表面上移動時 , 形狀會扭轉 , 就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 他們把自己當成點 , 用這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能讓它更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我肯定想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來這裡 。 真是太棒了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	富有傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古德會談到tacare和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助非洲小鎮的人們生活在受威脅的動物附近 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球性議題、污染、靈長類、科學、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德能協助人類和動物生活在一起 , 一起生活在一起 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 詹姆布 , 大便 , 大便 , 但是我們也可以 , 喔 , 喔 , ~ ~ ~ ~ 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , ~ ~ ~
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所做的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一代 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我要談的演講 , 來自昨天的zeray所留下的地點 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談論這個令人驚奇的三歲的澳大陸孩童 , 塞萊姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過歷史 , 家庭樹 , 透過dna基因檔案 , 來了解人類的歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 最近的路易斯利•萊克利 , 他把我設定在研究黑猩猩的路上 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時的狀況非常驚人 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你能告訴很多關於化石的外觀 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 關於他們如何生活方式 , 和他們共存的各種工藝品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不是化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在這個相當常見的理論 , 如果我們發現最接近的生物親戚 , 最接近的物種 , 和人類 , 可能這些行為在七百萬年前出現 , 人類和人類的祖先中出現了類似的行為 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特徵帶到古老、古老的過去 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看今天在教科書上處理人類進化的教科書 , 你常常會發現人們對於黑猩猩的行為有多早期的行為 , 基於黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	他們比其他生物更像我們 , 在ted會議中 , 我們已經聽說過這件事 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以對我來說 , 黑猩猩跟我們一樣 , 在某種程度上 , 牠們的行為 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每個黑猩猩都有自己的性格 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們一個名字 , 他們可以活到60年或更多 , 雖然我們認為大部分人可能不會在野外活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃爾茲先生 , 當她11或12歲時 , 她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她的嬰兒每五或六年就有一個嬰兒 , 長期以來的兒童依賴度 , 當孩子在晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後騎在她身上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 長久以來的童年時期對黑猩猩來說很重要 , 就像我們一樣 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	在不同形式的動物演化中 , 大腦會變得更複雜 , 所以我們發現 , 在個人的人生史中 , 學習扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間觀察他們的長輩做了些什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 這種方式 , 目前在非洲各個不同黑猩猩族族群中所看到的不同工具使用行為 , 研究這些人是如何從一個世代到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和實踐 , 這樣我們就能將這些工具的行為描述為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口頭的語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 很多都是相似的 , 甚至是相同的 , 與我們同類的 , 形成在同一個情境中 。 打招呼黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也親吻 , 握手 , 背對對方張貼 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	他們會變動 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多同情心的例子 , 前提是愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 像我們一樣 , 他們的本質有著黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘酷 , 甚至是最原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是針對鄰近社群的個體來指導 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常的激烈 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比起任何其他生物 , 已經協助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間沒有明顯的線條 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們觀察到的更加模糊 , 它一直變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究還在繼續下去 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 活在野外的複雜社交生活 , 協助我們了解到 , 我們是其中的一部分 , 而非我們共享這個星球的驚人動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	很遺憾地發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空氣中拍的照片 , 展示給各位看一片森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時 , 我飛越整個區域 , 大約16年前 , 發現 , 在公園外面 , 這片森林 , 在1960年間 , 幾乎沒有破壞 , 沿著坦桑尼卡湖湖岸的東岸 , 那個地方很小 , 30平方的山羊全國公園 , 那個問題出現在我腦海 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當住在全國公園附近的人在掙扎生存時 , 我們要如何拯救這些有名的黑猩猩 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人住在那兒 , 比起土地還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加了 , 來自緬甸和來自剛果湖的難民數 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常窮的人 , 他們負擔不起從別處購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種非常全面的方法 , 來改善住在公園附近的村莊裡的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從十二個村莊開始 , 現在是24個村莊 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探究它 , 但它包含了樹木護理工業 , 目前最適合農業的方法 , 幾乎是沙漠土地 , 落在這些山上 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 防止土壤侵蝕 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	恢復過度使用的農地的方式 , 這樣兩年內 , 就能再生生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	協助村民從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群女性合作 , 提供她們的機會給微型貸款 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們有 , 如同全世界的案例 , 世界上有95%的貸款都回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權女性 , 與教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓他們能完成中等學校 , 清楚了解到 , 全世界的女性教育都在改善 , 家庭規模的降低 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 保育計畫正在進行中 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的情況是 , 住在這24個村莊的農夫 , 而不是把我們看成一群白人來研究一大群猴子 , 順道一提 , 許多人現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始了坦尚尼亞計劃時 , 一個坦尚尼亞的團隊進入村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民談話 , 問他們感興趣的是什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們有興趣保育嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層被砍伐 , 所以土壤的侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展我們所謂的 「 大型gombe生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園外的一個地方 , 向外延伸到這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意把百分之十到二十的土地放到高地上 , 所以 , 再一次 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩就會有葉皮廊 , 通過這些路徑 , 牠們可以在國家公園外外的其他遺傳團體中與其他的遺傳團體互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們把它複製在非洲的其他地方 , 在其他地方 , 面對極端人口壓力的荒野地區 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們剛才討論過的 , 前幾天的ted演講 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有很大的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的居民住在土地上 , 不那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍樹時 , 你就把土壤開放到風中 , 因為絕望的人口減少了更多的樹木 , 所以他們可以試著種食物給自己和家人 , 有什麼事情會發生 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題 , 不僅僅是非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家 , 甚至到處都是 , 我們在地球上做些什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.威爾遜說 , 如果這個星球上每一個人都以普通歐洲人或美國人的標準生活 , 我們需要三個新的行星 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說的是四個 。 但是我們沒有他們 , 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事呢 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 這裡 , 我們是最聰明的人 , 可以走在地球上 , 帶著非凡的大腦 , 可以用這些ted會議來說明的科技 , 但卻毀了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決策之前 , 常常坐在一旁問自己: 「 這決定如何影響我們七個世代 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 主要的決策 , 我不是特別談論非洲 , 但已開發國家主要的決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是基於 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決策會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始環遊非洲時 , 談到黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林 , 我了解到 , 非洲有多少問題可以在過去的殖民地剝削之門上 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外面旅行 , 在歐洲演講 , 在美國 , 和亞洲談話 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我在說的那種 , 我在說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水水也許是我們本世紀所面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都有農業、工業和家庭家庭用品的污染 , 那些仍然被全世界噴灑的化學物 , 似乎無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林會被砍下來 ; 像海嘯這樣的效應會變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤侵蝕 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無能為力的化石燃料 , 伴隨著其他溫室氣體 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地 , 人們開始相信氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	影響更糟糕的窮人 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經被影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱的情況更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水和加油 , 造成貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在一個土地無法支援的地區 , 住在土地上的人數太貧窮 , 無法購買食物 , 無法搬走 , 因為整片土地已經退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化的哭泣 , 哭泣 , 哭泣的 , 正如最後一棵樹被砍下來的一樣 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都如此 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我並不意外 , 我遇見過這麼多年輕人似乎失去希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這個非凡聰明的大腦之間有某種區別嗎 ? 這種區分出了ted科技的表現 , 而人的心 ? 用非科學的術語來說 , 愛和同情的說法 , 是否有一些區別 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上 , 他們不是憂鬱或冷漠 , 或痛苦 , 或憤怒 。 他們說: 「 或多或少 , 」 他們說: 「 我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 我們沒有任何能做的事 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我就會想 , 自從我年紀開始 , 我就感到這種美麗的星球 , 我感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這個計畫引發了這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 由坦尚尼亞開始 , 現在已經散播到全世界的97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根是建立公司基金會的 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	槍擊似乎很小 ; 要到達太陽 , 牠們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為我們在地球上所遇到的問題 , 環境和社會上的所有問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有數十萬名年輕人可以突破 , 讓這個更美好的世界 , 讓所有生物都能活得更好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的重要訊息:我們每一個人都能做出改變 , 每天都有 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每個人 , 我們都有選擇 , 選擇我們想要做出什麼樣的差異 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	貧窮的人沒有選擇 , 由我們決定改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體都選擇了三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年紀多大 , 而在哪個國家 , 不管他們在城市或鄉村 , 不管他們是怎樣的專案 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有從幼稚園到大學的計畫 , 越來越多的成年人開始自己的根與芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體選擇 , 在他們之間 , 三種不同的計畫 , 讓這個更美好的世界變得更好 , 認知這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	其中一項計畫是要協助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能的話 , 他們就能籌錢來協助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一個項目是要協助動物 , 不僅僅是野生動物 , 家庭動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個項目是要協助大家分享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	所有這一切 , 都要傳達一個訊息 , 就是學習在我們自己的和平和和諧中 , 在我們的家庭中 , 在我們的社區中 , 國家、文化、宗教之間 , 和我們之間 , 和自然界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 , 我們不能以我們現在的速度摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個行星 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	就在非洲這裡 , 挑選一個或兩個項目 , 那些根源和槍擊團體正在進行 , 只有一個或兩個項目 , 在坦尚尼亞 , 烏干達 , 南非 , 剛果大廈 , 獅子山共和國 , 喀麥隆 , 還有其他團體 。 如我說的 , 在世界上97個國家 , 這裡已經有97個國家了 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 用雞蛋 , 把雞蛋賣給少量的雞蛋 , 或只用它們餵飽他們的家人 , 感受到驕傲和賦權的感覺 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依賴其他的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理協助 , 來培養士兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣的項目 , 就是把它們從自己身上帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以現在沒有更多的根源和芽時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病/愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要因素 , 與較年長的孩子對話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	沒想過懷孕之類的 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的心聲 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你見過你的黑猩猩數量下降 , 數量從一百萬 , 在這個世紀的轉捩點 , 到現在 , 沒有超過十五萬人 , 和許多其他動物相同 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經有森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 對吧 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中一個是很棒的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我一直很興奮 , 終於 , 來到人們談論堆肥的廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把這些水沖到熔梯底 , 真的很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到可再生能源迫切地重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們在乎我們的孩子這個星球嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有孩子或孫子孫女 , 姪女 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們 , 身為世界各地的精英們 , 我們可以為它做點什麼 , 我們可以做出選擇 , 做為我們日常生活的方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做出這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我的孩子 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或其他的東西 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 與人的心情結合 , 我們加入世界各地 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted所能幫助的 , google幫助我們 , esri在gombe國家公園上繪製的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有我們能使用的技術 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	你今天下午已經聽過它了 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們必須要看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由是令人驚訝的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一塊絕對被摧毀的區域 , 用時間 , 或許有些幫助它可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	一個例子就是一個治療方案 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我跟你說 , 看似死掉的樹木 , 如果你停止砍柴它們 , 不用砍柴 , 因為你有木材 , 五年內 , 你就可以有一棵30英尺的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在絕種的邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它很鼓舞人心 。 它帶我到我最後的希望類別 , 在過去的兩天 , 我們已經聽到了這麼多的希望:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 使你認為會被貧窮、疾病或任何人所欺騙 , 不論如何 , 都可以把自己拉出去 , 帶到社會中 , 把他們的一部分改變 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 非洲有一兩個人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一份很長的清單 , 但顯然 , 曼德拉的名單從十七年的硬體勞動力開始 , 23年的監禁 , 讓他能夠寬恕他的國家 , 讓他無法帶走種族隔離的邪惡政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa在奈及利亞 , 他採用了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都盡了最好的辦法 , 被處決 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人如此的靈感 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們年輕非洲人所需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 今天我也聽到了其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以 , 我非常感謝這個機會 , 再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起討論這些事情 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後 , 一位年輕女子正在參加這場會議中心的年輕人 , 我今天遇見了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 和她的證書 。 她是根和槍擊隊員 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在darrsalaam的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這幫助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 去見見她是非常非常令人興奮的 , 看到一個例子 , 說明了年輕人如何被賦權 , 因為他們有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩有一些艱難的事實 , 關於海洋和生活中的塑膠污染 , 以及一些想法 , 如何讓自己脫離塑膠世界 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命藍色、海洋、塑膠、塑膠、塑膠等議題 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染塑膠污染的困難真相:
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 我把塑膠袋剪下來 , 把它們縫起來 , 作為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 過去二十年 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二、三維的零件、雕塑、裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	與塑膠合作 , 大約在我頭八年之後 , 有些作品開始裂開 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣 , 這種日常生活就跟我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在教我自己更進一步的關於塑膠 , 我發現這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成較小的部分 , 因為它永遠是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多東西都在海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	然後 , 在過去的幾年 , 我學到太平洋垃圾場和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是 , 很多人的第一個反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得要去外面清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我發明了一個建議 , 和一艘貨船一起出去 , 和兩艘委員會的漁船 , 一台拖車 , 一台拖車 , 一台冰冷的機器 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是 , 出去看健身房 , 提高對於這個議題的認知 , 開始把塑膠晶片切成碎片 , 將它切成磚塊 , 以便能被用來當作已開發社區的材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些真的去過健身房的人聊天 , 開始研究海洋環境裡的塑膠問題 , 然後就這樣做 , 我意識到 , 清理它會是非常小的一滴水滴 , 跟世界各地的生產量相比 , 我需要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉外表 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切割單一、可分解的塑膠 , 它們每天都要進入海洋環境 , 以全球的規模來進行 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這個 , 我發現我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 還在太平洋的正中間 , 我所學到的 , 現在有11個健身房 , 可能是世界上五個大海裡的塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是我所關心的塑膠垃圾 , 還有超市的塑膠垃圾堆 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都包裝在塑膠上 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是塑膠的包裝 , 即使是在健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我擔心塑膠和毒素 , 從塑膠到我們身上 , 進入我們的身體 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他人一起研究這個議題 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多計畫正在進行 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的海底有80% ~ 90%的海洋碎片 , 我們在海洋中發現的就是塑膠 , 那麼我們為什麼不把它稱為它 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	再回收每個人的書 , 來結束他們關於永續和綠化的書 , 用回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個垃圾桶 , 你不需要再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	實際的情況是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠的回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細看 , 尤其是當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分的瓶子只會被循環循環 , 或被運到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被循環循環轉變成更少的東西 , 雖然玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或者可以再次使用 , 塑膠瓶也不能再次成為塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們看到的另一件事 , 請大家想想 , 我們把第四個r加在 「 縮減、再利用、回收 」 前面 , 三個r , 拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	每當可能發生時 , 都拒絕使用單一和可分解的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些則是非常老式的學科 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用這些裝置 , 而不是魅惑和洗碗容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人做一個服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易就拿起一瓶無汙染的瓶子或玻璃瓶 , 假如你在旅行 , 你忘了把你的不確定瓶子裝滿 , 用水或過濾水 , 和購買塑膠瓶 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想我想要向大家說的是我知道你們對這個議題的了解很多 , 就是這在海洋裡是個很大的問題 , 但這是我們創造出來的消費者 , 我們可以解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以透過提高人們意識到這個議題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能地選擇單一塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這條幹細胞切入海洋中 , 這樣一來 , 拯救海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這位來自麻省理工學院的皮提梅斯實驗室的示範 , 由帕拉.密里所引發的 , 是ted的buzz , 是一個可穿戴的裝置 , 用來與環境深刻的互動 , 想像 「 少數 」 的報告 , 再來 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 介面設計 , 技術 , 科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派特•瑪斯和帕拉夫•米特•米特•狄摩斯 , 第六感是第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很感興趣 , 關於我們能否演化或發展出第六感一種感覺 , 一種讓我們能無縫、容易取得資訊 , 或存在的資訊 , 可能會有相關性 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 不論我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 今天的手機不是已經做到的嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted認識某人時 , 這當然是最頂尖的網絡網絡地點 , 你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能拿出我的手機和谷歌嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你去超級市場時 , 你站在那裏 , 站在那裏 , 大型的衛生紙 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 進入一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的廁所論文中哪些是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 可以協助我們做出最佳的決策 , 來做下一步該做的事 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究團隊開發了一系列的發明 , 以一種簡單的方式 , 不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡要揭露我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 仍然是處理過程的一份工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	我現在正穿著這個裝置 , 我們已經將它與架上的零件混合在一起 , 順便說一下 , 當時只花了350美金 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著照相機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式、電池驅動的投影系統 , 裡面有一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡通訊我的手機 , 可以當作溝通和計算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這個影片中 , 我們看到我的學生pranavavidry , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走向任何表面 , 用他的手和投影在他面前的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤四根指頭 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著一個簡單的標記帽子 , 可以辨識出來 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更固定的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色來畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上追蹤了這四隻手指 , 並認出他所製作的任何姿勢 , 例如 , 他可以去看長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出象徵性的手勢 , 比如 「 拍照 」 姿勢 , 接著拍一張在你面前的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何牆上 , 投影所有他拍攝的照片 , 透過它們 , 整理它們 , 再把它們變大 , 諸如此類 , 再一次使用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 有些人可能兩年前來到這裡 , 看到傑夫•漢的示範 , 有些人可能會想: 「 這不像微軟表面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用天然手勢來互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以使用任何表面 , 你可以走向任何表面 , 包括沒有其他東西可以使用 , 和這個投影資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是可攜式的 , 也可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是行動行動 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差別是 , 在大眾生產中 , 明天的成本會比現今的手機還要高 , 實際上 , 包裝的效果會比我脖子周圍的這個版本更大 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但 , 除此之外 , 除了讓一些人活出你的幻想 , 像湯姆•克魯斯在 「 少數報告報告 」 中 , 湯姆•克魯斯的幻想之外 , 我們之所以感到興奮 , 是因為它真的可以作為這六個感知裝置的其中一個 , 讓你能了解你面前的任何東西 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到pranav進入超市 , 他正在購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統可以辨識出他撿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橘色光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個特別的選擇是他個人標準的好選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想要有廁所論文 , 裡面有最多白血 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿到亞馬遜的評分 , 就會被投射在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是朱安的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順便說一下 , 亞馬遜的評分很棒 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕拉夫把書的頁面翻過來 , 還能看到書本讀者留言的額外資訊 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉向某個特定的頁面 , 他會發現一個可能是一位朋友的註冊專家 , 給他一點額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的事件的錄音 , 可以得到最新的運動分數 。
this is a more controversial one .	這更具爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某人互動時 , 也許你可以看到標籤的單字雲 , 和那個人在他們的部落格和個人網頁上有相關的字 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機有興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你到機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機道 , 它可以告訴你你的飛機被延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 諸如此類 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的狀況 , 就像你手臂上的手臂上的手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展的第六種感官 , 可以給我們無縫的資訊 , 讓所有我們可能接觸到的事物都能取得相關的資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生pranav , 就像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。

and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在未來的10年內 , 我們會在這裡 , 終極第六感的大腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲利斯•羅德里格茲和阿卡拉•瓦菲有強大的友誼 , 來自於無法想像的損失 。 羅德里格茲的兒子在世貿中心被殺害 , 發生在2001年9月11日 ; 伊瓦菲的兒子塞羅•莫薩伊被定罪 , 同時也在尋找和平的過程中 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位母親能了解並尊重 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球性議題、政治、文化、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11的療癒:找到寬恕的母親 , 友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格斯:我們今天在這裡 , 是因為我們有許多人認為非比尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在對我們來說卻很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到我兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	直到36小時後 , 我們才知道他是否死了 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道這是政治性的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家會以我們兒子的名字來命名 , 歐蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 透過震驚 , 恐怖的震驚 , 以及我們生命中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有被毒害 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , zacariasmoussaui被指出六種陰謀謀殺恐怖主義 , 美國政府向他尋求死刑 , 如果被定罪的話 , 我丈夫和我公開對抗這件事 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些 , 透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者的家人聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到艾卡哈 , 當她的兒子被告知時 , 我心想: 「 什麼是勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想要在我強壯時遇到那位女士 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深刻的悲慟中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是個受害者時 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被控告時 , 她沒有得到那樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , 阿卡哈現在會告訴你這怎麼來的 。
