aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是尚卡拉雅山脈的祖母 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我詢問了人權組織 , 讓我聯絡受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我到五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了菲利斯 , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我遭受許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacarias的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然受苦 , 因為我的兒子就像他活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她為她的兒子哭泣了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否活著 , 我不知道他是否受折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以 , 我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對於所有的女性 , 給予生命的所有母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須要有手工 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 對我們女性 , 對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我談暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校 , 和年輕的穆斯林女孩談 , 讓他們不接受和她們的意願結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我能拯救一個年輕女孩 , 避免她們結婚和受苦 , 像我一樣 , 這樣好 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	帕特:我想說 , 我從阿卡哈學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們和其他家庭成員一起開會 , 那是一個非常私人的會議 , 因為那是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕那個國家的超級同性戀 , 那些我們家人 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都如此緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她想要和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們想要見到她 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們想要彼此什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字之前 , 或任何東西之前 , 我們都擁抱和哭泣了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個充滿支持的圈子裡 , 和協助 , 來自人們在這種相互關聯的圈子裡 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是否有罪惡感 , 或無辜 , 但我想告訴各位 , 我對你的家庭發生了什麼事感到抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道受苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有犯罪 , 一個人應該要公平地做懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她用那樣的方式向我們伸出援手 , 那時 , 我想要說 , 那是個冰架製造者 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來 , 我們都會說出我們的故事 , 身為人類 , 我們都把故事連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到下午的尾聲 , 午餐後大約三小時 , 我們會覺得好像我們永遠認識彼此一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不僅可以在這些現況下變得如此慷慨 , 和當時的狀況 , 以及她兒子所做的事 , 還有她兒子的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱難的人生 , 從一個完全不同的文化和環境 , 來自我自己的環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常重視 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都和害怕對方有關 , 但要做這個步驟 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	誰還能見到我不知道的 , 又或者我和誰不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , 阿卡哈 , 你有幾個字來做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說 , 我們得要試著去了解其他人 , 其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須是慷慨的 , 你的心一定是慷慨的 , 你的心靈一定是慷慨的 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要容忍 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們會一起生活在和平和尊重中 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多地方缺乏乾淨的飲用水 。 工程師麥可•普雷特•普特查德做了一些事情 , 發明了可攜帶的生命過濾器 , 可以在幾秒鐘內 , 讓最具反思性的飲用水 。 這是2009年tedglobal的一個令人驚奇的示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、demo、設計、全球性議題、發明、技術、水、水、水 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelpritchard的水過濾器會過濾骯髒的水 , 飲用的水很不可思議 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	首先是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在 , 我看到你們都很享受在研討會上所提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這來自安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果是來自這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	接著統計數字會說 , 在座有一半的人會因為腹瀉而受苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談過很多關於統計數據 , 以及所有人的安全飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎沒有經歷過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	那是因為 , 用目前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法思考解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以 , 我們關掉:我們、政府和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想用不同的角度來看 , 問題已經解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 自從我在說話之後 , 世界各地有一萬三千人正在受腹瀉所苦 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛死了 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了救世主的瓶子 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節過後一天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯爆發的災難報導 , 在電視上演出 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子和幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝污染的水或死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這真的讓我印象深刻 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風衝向美國 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	我心想: 「 好吧 , 這是第一個世界國家 , 看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道花了五天才把水送到超級迷嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相射擊電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我在車庫待了很多時間 , 在接下來的幾週和幾個月 , 在我的廚房裡 , 我太太太太太太太太太太太太太太太太太太太很討厭 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想出了這個 , 救命的瓶子 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來做一點科學研究 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在救世主之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約有200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	一個200奈米的細菌會穿過200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這絕對會穿過那200奈米的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命維持水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有任何東西能通過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下 。
would you like to see that ?	你想要看到嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間把這些設定好 , 所以我想我應該這麼做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在牛津的精緻城市裡 。
so someone's done that up .	所以 , 有人這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	最好的牛津城 , 我所做的是 , 我去過河邊的cherwell , 河流的thames , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我想 , 要知道 , 如果我們在孟加拉的洪水區中央 , 水就不像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以 , 我做了一些東西來加入它 。
and this is from my pond .	這是從我的池塘出來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞到這首歌 , 攝影師.
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只會把這些倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	michaelpritchard:好的 , 我們有一些來自污水廠的跑道 。
so i'm just going to put that in there .	所以 , 我要把它放進去 。
put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 , 就這樣 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	其他的部分和碎片 , 把它們放進去 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我有個來自我的朋友的兔子的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	我們也要把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	救命瓶子的運作其實很簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水拉起來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個斷層給你們看 , 讓你們看一下吧 。 來看看吧 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	那還不夠髒 。 讓我們稍微攪一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好吧 , 我要用這個非常骯髒的水 , 把它放進去 。 你想喝一杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好 , 開始吧 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶壺倒下 , 無菌的飲用水就會出去 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我必須要快點 。 好 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	就這樣 , 注意電 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	這是安全的 , 無菌飲用水 。
there you go chris .	你去克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它嚐起來是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯的節目 , 其他節目的其他節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 , 世界各地數以千計的人都使用了生命安全瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它會維持6 , 000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它被激發時 , 使用失敗的科技 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把卡車出去 , 把一個新插進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	這對6 , 000公升有益 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾週後 , 我們成立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入營地 , 取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時 , 會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病散播 , 需要更多資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題就在於自我表達 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考方式 , 運送這些東西 , 人們就可以留下去 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自己做無菌飲用水 , 開始重建家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這並不需要自然災害來運作 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	使用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 實在太昂貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算機上計算出數字時 , 你就跑出來了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這就是 " 思考的不同 " 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	不用運送水 , 用人造流程來做這件事 , 咱們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她把水從那裡取出來 , 把水淡化 , 免費運送到那裡 , 把水丟到山上 , 河流和河流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水邊 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的只是讓它變得不穩定 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用救命瓶子 。
or we could use one of these .	或者 , 我們可以用其中一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry的罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理2萬5千公升的水 , 足夠四個家庭 , 三年來 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天半分錢來跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 用水來處理水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四個小時 , 才能收集水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	它們可以從附近的來源取得 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以 , 只要八十億美金 , 我們就能達到千禧年目標的目標 , 目的就是要讓沒有安全的飲用水的人數減少 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	要把這套套套用在外國援助上 , 英國政府每年花費大約12億英鎊 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在這裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了2000億美元 , 每個人都可以取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以 , 每年有三十五億人受苦 , 結果 , 每年有兩百萬名兒童死亡 , 會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashown宣稱我們生活在歷史上 , 歷史上 , 權力從來沒有改變過的方式 。 在tedxbrussel的演講中 , 他排擠了三個重大的全球變革 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球性議題 , 政治 , 世界文化 , 文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球的權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在19世紀末 , 有一個非常有名的英文詩人寫了一首詩 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教堂的大腦會被說是 「 回應 」 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩說: 「 在夏天的伊德爾山丘上 , 拉著溪流的流動 , 哈克 , 我聽到遠方的鼓聲 , 像在夢裡的聲音 , 遠在地球上 , 很近 , 越來越大聲 , 在路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物 , 士兵們遊行 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩歌感興趣的人 , 詩的詩是 「 一名購物商店的lad 」 , 由a.e.休士曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 休士人了解的 , 你也在尼爾森交響樂中聽到了 , 尼爾森的漫長 , 熱 , silvan的夏天 , 在19世紀的穩定性中 , 我們即將進入一個令人害怕的歷史中 , 當權力改變時 , 我們即將進入一個令人害怕的時代 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些都是月經 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著亂流 , 經常都是血液 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我對你傳達的訊息是 , 我相信我們已經被譴責了 , 只要你相信 , 我們生活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當這些被建立的權力開始改變了 , 世界上存在的新看法 , 新勢力就開始形成了 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚的看到 , 幾乎每次都非常亂 , 非常艱難的時光 , 經常非常血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順道一提 , 每個世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你也許會主張 , 最後一次發生了 , 猶太人也來了 , 教堂也覺得 , 當權力從舊的國家 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 跨越大西洋 , 到美國的新興勢力 , 美國一世紀初期 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 進入真空中 , 以前歐洲人使用過的權力 , 都是在上世紀的兩場血腥災難中 , 第一場 , 第二個則是:兩場偉大的世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	maozedong以前把他們稱為歐洲內戰 , 可能更準確地形容他們 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談的是三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一種 , 第一種是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二 , 關於一些新的維度我想提一下 , 這種現象從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 咱們來談談全球發生的權力轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	現今正在發生的事情 , 某種意義上 , 令人害怕 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經見識過希臘的權力轉移到羅馬和歐洲文明文明的權力轉移但我們卻看到一些稍微不同的東西
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力的發展不僅僅是從國家轉移到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也在垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今正在發生的情況是 , 那些被監禁的權力 , 被關在法律的規則上 , 在這個國家的制度中 , 現在已經遷移到極大的全球舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	我們談到全球化市場的全球化 , 但事實上 , 它是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級上 , 權力的責任主題是法律的規則 , 在國際舞台上 , 它不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球的權力 , 如今的權力 , 網際網路的力量 , 衛星廣播的力量 , 金錢改變了這個巨大的貨幣的力量 , 流通了這筆巨大的貨幣 , 交易所需的金錢額 , 應該要有金錢的改變者 , 假如 , 金融的推測者 , 最近 , 把我們都帶到我們的膝蓋 , 超大的金融企業的力量 , 會發展出更多的國家 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個沒有規範的全球空間 , 而不是法律的規則 , 而在這個地方 , 人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在 , 這裝備了強大的位置 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	那些在沒有限制的情況下 , 經營最有權力的人 , 總是可以適應的 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 更早 , 或後來 , 沒有規範的空間 , 不只受到你想要的國際貿易、網際貿易等等的事物 , 還有你不希望國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的事物 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些居住著太空的人 , 甚至可以攻擊你最具代表性的城市 , 一個九月的早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 四百萬美金中有60%被帶到911恐怖襲擊的金融塔中 , 911恐怖襲擊的金融塔 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這個空間 , 大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播 , 來抵禦他們的毒品 , 來破壞我們的系統 , 以及我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久後 , 不久後 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力必須遵守的地方 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	假如這是我相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是全球化的權力 , 那麼我們這個時代所面臨的挑戰就是把統治權帶入全球空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 在我們未來的數十年 , 未來的數十年 , 將會成為更大或更少的渦輪 , 我們能達成這個目標:把治理帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生女士們 , 女士們 , 不太可能透過更多聯合國機構來完成 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得要發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方法 , 可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 當談到全球性空間的治理時 , 我的猜測是 , 這不會發生在聯合國的制度上 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 它會透過強大的力量結合在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統 , 以條約為基礎的協議 , 來管理全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你觀察 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 但 , 強大到能容納最強大的國家 , 美國 , 如果必要的話 , 會考慮到會計 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:努力創造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國:我們現在知道 , 我們得要組成一個制度 , 能夠把治理的機構帶到金融空間 , 來做財務推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20的原因 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 等一下我們會再回來談談 , 如果把最強大的力量結合在一起 , 以條約為基礎的制度來填補治治理的空間 , 那麼 , 弱者的情況會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 等一下我們再回來談談 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要通過這些亂流的傳遞時間 , 或更亂的傳遞 , 那麼 , 我們的成功會大幅地取決於我們的能力 , 將合理的治理傳播到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和觀眾談這樣的話題 , 但權力不只是垂直轉換 , 它也在轉換地平線 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會主張 , 文明的歷史 , 人類的歷史 , 已經在海洋周圍的文明和地中海最初的文明結合在一起 , 比較近期的文明在大西洋周圍的西方勢力 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 我們現在看到了一種基本的權力轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離大西洋的國家 , 聚集在太平洋的邊緣 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這從經濟方面開始 , 但這一直都是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的增長 , 發生在世界上其他的發展中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	其實 , 我認為這不是從西方移轉到東方的轉變 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於值得的 , 美國在未來的10年 , 15年內 , 將仍然是地球上最強大的國家 , 但她持有的權力的情境現在已經徹底改變了 , 徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正從50年來 , 最不尋常的歷史中 , 在歷史中 , 我們有一個完全獨立的獨立世界 , 每一針都必須針對它的位置來參考華盛頓一個世界最好的英雄 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的情況更正常 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多向分化的世界出現了 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直都是我們世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會維持最強大的國家 , 但他們會是世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到中國的替代權力中心 , 當然 , 我的猜測是 , 中國的優勢不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國在自由化經濟後 , 開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但這是個不同的討論 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 世界現在看起來真的 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 更像19世紀的歐洲人 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀 , 歐洲是英國外交部長 , 哥倫•坎普 , 曾經形容它是 「 歐洲人的權力音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡 , 一個五面體的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在平衡上演 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林一起 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供反平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由單向世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的盟友 , 北約 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的權力意味著固定聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但有多種權力對立意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們將會看到我們的聯盟並非固定的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	英國外交部長坎普 , 曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有普通盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到 , 即使我們在西方的西方國家都能伸出援手 , 還得伸出去 , 超越大西洋的力量 , 來和他人聯盟 , 只要我們想要把事情搞定在世界上 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家並不夠好 ; 我們得要把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個案例中 , 我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是最後一次 , 西方嘗試自己做的時候 , 我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經達到了400年末期的開始 , 我說400年了 , 因為那是奧托曼帝國的結尾 , 西方的力量 , 西方的制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 世界各地的每個角落都可以發聲和發聲 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不再是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家結合了布雷頓森林組織 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金 , 解決了問題 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在他人身上打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造出g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經達到400年的末期了 , 那時西方的勢力已經夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與和平協會 , 全世界的多邊和平協會 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色的貝雷下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 在聯合國的指揮下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大的海軍總署 , 要處理索馬利海盜的問題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國人指導內容 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是民族主義者 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要讓海道開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	日漸地 , 我們要和那些不分享價值觀的人做生意 , 但在當下 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的觀點 , 現在正在興起這個世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	這是第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	現今 , 在我們的現代世界裡 , 由於網路 , 因為人們在這裡所談論的各種事物 , 所有事物都與所有事物連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在被封鎖 , 作為國家 , 作為個體 , 以一種從未發生過的案例 , 從來沒有發生過的案例 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是要管理國家之間的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被緊密關起來了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥有豬流感 , 查爾斯•高爾飛機 , 24小時後 , 遇到了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 全部的崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯的階梯 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、深切的相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨立行動的概念 , 不是和他人連結 , 和他人合作 , 不再是個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為國家的行為既不受限於自己 , 也不足以控制自己的國家 , 因為國家外在國家的影響已經開始影響他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最小帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的國防 , 只有一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強壯 , 我們的海軍有多強大 , 我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那時 , 敵人在牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人在牆壁內 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想談談我國家的國防部 , 我必須和衛生部門談談 , 因為流行病對我的保安 , 我得要和農業部長談談 , 因為食物保障對我的保安 , 我得要和工業部長談談 , 因為 , 希臘基礎建設的脆弱 , 現在我們從網路戰爭中看到的威脅 , 我們的敵人 , 現在 , 要談談談七個國家的恐怖分子 , 因為 , 我們的敵人 , 現在 , 要談談談談起我們國家的恐怖主義 , 要談談談談到我在777個國家的家 , 因為 , 在我國內 , 在我國內的國內 , 在我國內的國內 , 國內 , 國內 , 國內的國內 , 國內 , 國內的國內的國內的國內 , 和國內 , 和國內的國內的國內 , 和國內的國內的國內的國內的國內的國內的國內的國內 , 和國內外交流行政權利益處在國內的國內 , 政府和國內的國內 ,
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是一個國家的安全性 , 對於士兵和國防部來說 , 這不再只是一個問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	把它們鎖在一起的制度是它的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這說明了非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直的階層階層 , 任務的專業化 , 指令結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商業界 , 各位先生女士 , 都知道我們這個時代的典型結構就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	你的網絡網絡的能力很重要 , 不管你政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我有關阿凡達第一個法則 , 第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明過這些法律 ; 如果第三定律的話 , 聽起來比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdn的第三定律是 , 在現代 , 所有東西都和所有東西連結在一起 , 最重要的是你能做的 , 就是你能和他人做的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊註冊 , 不論你是企業 , 都是你的運輸點 , 你的連接點 , 你的網絡能力 , 和他人連結 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白這一點 , 在工業上 , 政府也不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 各位先生女士 , 我們現在就被封鎖在一個以前從來沒有這麼相同的情況下 , 那也是我們彼此命運的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主導我們 , 把我們當作 「 安排國家 」 的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我很安全 ; 我的盟友 , 像nato , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我很安全 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是案例了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的爆發 , 意味著 , 我和敵人有了命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我是個外交官 , 在1970年代 , 我和日內瓦的蘇聯談判時 , 我和蘇聯談 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道 , 我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩方都了解到 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的大障礙之一 , 是以色列 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人不明白他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 各位先生女士 , 先生們 , 過去的願景和詩人的主張 , 變成我們必須認真看待公共政策的重要性 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•唐恩的偉大詩 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 送給誰 , 不用花招 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是孤島 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	答案是: 「 每個男人的死亡都會影響我 , 因為我參與了人類 , 不要去問誰的鈴聲 , 要花錢 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰•唐恩來說 , 道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 對我們生存的方程式有一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽的生活和健康的路 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究這個世界的 「 藍色區域 」 , 他們的長者和維京人一起生活 , 在tedxtc , 他分享了9種常見的飲食習慣 , 讓他們能在一百歲以前流逝 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、科學、科學、科學、科學、生物、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹•布伊特納:要如何活到100+1+2 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥的雙胞胎研究成立了約10%的比例 , 在某些生物限制下 , 人類的基因中 , 平均壽命只有10% 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由我們的生活方式來主導 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能得到丹歐長壽的公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘的飲食 , 或墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國da食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們 ,
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們什麼 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更久的情況 , 有很多困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松 , 還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是應該吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當談到供應時 , 你應該把它們拿來嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙或復育器呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	其中有目的嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性呢 ? 我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們要找到長壽的方法是和國家地理雜誌合作 , 國家老化研究所合作 , 找出四個人口統計的地區 , 地理上所定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一組專家到那裡去 , 用的方法來處理這些人所做的事 , 把跨文化的散播放下來 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	到頭來 , 我將要告訴各位那是多麼的煩擾 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想在長壽時 , 提到一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很努力 , 你可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國500000人當中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機率非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然它是美國成長最快的人口統計 , 但卻很難達到100% 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有為長壽而設計 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被訂定為 「 繁榮成功 」 的計畫 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起了大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁榮成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一代 , 孩子有孩子的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應完全消失 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是隻老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 也是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要達到一百歲 , 你不只需要一個非常好的生活方式 , 你也得贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療可以減緩、逆轉 , 甚至阻止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	耗盡了氧氣的大腦幾分鐘 , 這些腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 斷掉你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用白斑來排列 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用 「 t 」 來討論國家債務數據 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每8年就一次自轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉過來時 , 就會造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它會以指數的方式來建造 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像當時我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製它 , 讓朋友複製膠帶 , 很快地 , 錄音帶聽起來像垃圾一樣 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個125歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有任何東西可以減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約九十年 , 對女人來說 , 稍微多一點點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條路上 , 我們在桌上留下了大約12個好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們可以做到 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 它們會大多不受慢性疾病、心臟疾病、癌症 , 和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些缺失的年份 , 最好的方式是看看全世界的文化 , 真正體驗到它們的文化 , 在那裡 , 人們生活的年齡比我們生活的年齡還要高一百倍 , 比我們所處的還要高十倍 , 預期壽命多出十多年 , 中年的死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現在義大利海岸外大約125英里的藍色區域 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只有在高地上 , 一個叫努羅省的地區 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡的這個區域 , 男性壽命最長的地區 , 比美國這裡的百歲人多了十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只能到達一百歲 , 還能做到非凡的願景 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	十二歲的孩子 , 仍然騎著腳踏車去工作 , 開木頭 , 打敗一個比他們年輕六十歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實是回到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是種孤立的青銅文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的微不足道 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 偶爾會有規律、低強度的實體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要以植物為基礎 , 以牠們能帶到田野的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一條未開發的小麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂 , 由杜魯姆小麥製成 , 一種乳酪是由草食性動物所製成的 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 一種類型的酒 , 比世界上任何酒都多出三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會中最常見的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎是在24歲時高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 年紀越長 , 你就得到越多的平等 , 你得到的智慧就越多 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進沙丁尼亞的酒吧 , 而不是看到運動畫出了泳衣日曆 , 你看到的是月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不僅對你老化的父母有好處 , 讓他們和家人保持親近 , 差不多四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說 , 死亡率和疾病的比率也較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊發現了第二個藍色區塊 , 東京的南方約800英里 , 位於奧克納瓦的阿基比拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的零地點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們擁有世上最長的缺陷壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們很長一段時間 , 通常會在他們的睡眠中死亡 , 很快 , 通常 , 我會告訴你 , 在性交之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們活得比一般美國人的平均壽命還長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國有五倍的百歲人數 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的蟻群和乳癌的比例 , 在美國這裡的大型殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這種文化已經證明了這些數字很強烈地表示他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們和美國人一樣吃了大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起他們吃的東西 , 更顯著 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略可以避免過度使用 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:牠們會吃下較小的盤子 , 所以牠們通常會吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其提供家庭風格 , 不如你在說話時 , 你可以無心地吃東西 , 不用在櫃台上 , 把食物拿走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個30000年的廣告 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由混亂所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 哈拉 , 哈特 , 哈 , 哈 , 哈 , 海奇 , 飲食 。 」
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在吃飯之前會說 , 要提醒他們不要再吃下去 , 當他們的肚子滿了80% 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	要花大約半小時才能從你的肚子到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住 , 百分之八十的時間停止 , 它能讓你避免做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , 奧納瓦的社交建設有幾個社會建構 , 我們可以和長壽有關聯 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	15年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	現在我們只剩下一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運 , 在奧地納瓦出生 , 你就生在一個系統裡 , 自動有五十個朋友 , 和你在人生中旅行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai中 , 你預期會跟你談運氣 , 如果你遇到糟糕的話 , 孩子會生病 , 父母會死 , 總是有背後的人 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個獨特的摩艾族人 , 這五個女士已經在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生命分為兩區 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	一般來說 , 這意味著退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或下到亞利桑那去玩高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan語中 , 甚至沒有退休的詞語 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之 , 有一個字是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯一下 , 意思是 「 你早上醒來的原因 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的凱特大師來說 , 他的ikigai正帶著這種火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對於這一百歲的漁夫 , 一週持續捕魚魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所給我們一個問卷 , 給予百歲人 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們是非常文化的財富 , 那些問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對於這位102歲的老婦人 , 她的吉瓦伊僅是她的曾曾祖父 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101.5歲時分開 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 是什麼感覺 ? 拿著曾曾祖父的那種感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她的頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺好像跳進天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理位置的編輯希望我找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們在明尼蘇達的草原上 , 那裡有非常高比例的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國在加州羅馬林達州的第七天大冒險家中最長壽的人口 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	進步者是保守的方法家 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們會在星期六的星期五日落慶祝他們的安息日 , 直到星期六日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 24小時的庇護所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五種小習慣 , 傳達給他們非凡的長壽 , 相對來說 ,
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位先進女士而言 , 他們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更是男性 , 預期會比美國人多活11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	嚴格的研究 。 我認為它最具體的說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異性族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白色、黑色、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點就是一組非常小的生活習慣 , 讓他們在他們人生中 , 通常都是如此 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中取得他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	辛西亞:第一章是29年 , 上帝談到樂高和種子 , 再談談綠色植物 , 很明顯地 , 忽略了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們認真看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週有24小時 , 不管他們有多忙 , 他們工作的壓力有多大 , 孩子需要被驅動 , 他們會停止一切 , 專注在他們的神 , 他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 宗教中的無線電網 , 是大自然的走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這項技術的力量不是偶爾會完成 , 權力是每週都完成一輩子 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有一個很困難 。 沒有一個成本 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他的先進者交流 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個先進派對 , 你不會看到人們在游泳吉姆貝姆 , 或投入一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談論他們的下一本大自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻、可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這種文化讓埃爾斯•沃爾斯•威爾姆感到不舒服 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellworthwharewharem是97歲的
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是百萬富翁 , 但當一個包商想要6 , 000美元來建立一個隱私的柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那筆錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以在接下來的三天 , 他出去了一些水泥 , 四處挖洞 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可想而知 , 也許 , 在他第四天到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不像桌上的那個傢伙在做開心手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 每個月他仍然做二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	愛德華.羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 一早就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在周末 , 他喜歡在板子上裝上 , 丟下羅斯特尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她開始了她的日子 , 體重升高 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾被捲入到她的羅根尼托 , 她在聖貝納多高速公路上 , 在那裡 , 她仍然自願參加七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我參加了19次勤奮的探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你會遇過的唯一一個騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠卻沒有防曬霜的人 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我會告訴你 , 沒有任何冒險 , 比起騎士德頓的火星飛行器 , 沒有更多的冒險 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我尚未見面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有哪些共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們所做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功把它煮成九塊 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 從這次之後 , 我們做了兩個藍色區域的探險 , 而這些常見的偵測器則是對的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我將要說出一個問題 , 沒有一個是運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們設立了自己的生命 , 這樣他們會不斷地被放入實體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些100歲的okinawan女子們每天站在地面上 , 每天30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次旅行到商店 , 或教堂 , 或朋友家偶爾都會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以按下院門工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	燃燒卡路里和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做刻意的身體活動時 , 他們喜歡做他們喜歡的活動時 , 他們傾向走路 , 證明唯一能偷走認知衰退的方法 , 他們都傾向擁有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來建立自己的人生 , 讓他們有正確的前景 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間降低 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawannns有著這種祖先的傳奇 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你處在障礙或壓力之中 , 會引發一種叫 「 發炎性反應 」 的反應 , 這種反應和阿茲海默症的一切有關 , 有關心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢15分鐘 , 你就會把那個發炎狀態轉變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們用字彙來表示目的、ikigai , 和okinawanns一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的 , 他們在人生中活化 , 值7年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天喝一點點酒 , 而不是賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向吃植物為基礎的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	並不是說牠們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免過度捕撈 , 小東西會把它們從對的時間點消失 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 所有這些的基礎就是它們連結的方式 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人放在第一批 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老年父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都屬於信仰型社群 , 值四到十四年的預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是 , 他們也屬於對部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是天生就在他們身邊 , 或是他們自動地與對的人在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗蘭明罕研究中得知 , 如果三個最好的朋友都過胖了 , 會有百分之五十的機率會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人聊天 , 隨著時間 , 會造成可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對重組的概念是身體活動 , 鮑林 , 或彈奏曲棍球 , 騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝點酒 , 但不太多 , 他們吃得好 , 他們很投入 , 信任和值得信賴 , 這會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 , 世界歷史上沒有飲食 , 超過2%的人口數量 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 , 通常是十月份完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到長壽時 , 藥丸或其他藥丸都沒有短期的單詞修復 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你思考這件事時 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 或許你能做的最重要的事情 , 多年來 , 及生活 。 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	加州的導電機 , 一扇窗戶 , 從明顯的轉換到烏托克 , 轉換成開關 ; 一個製造音樂的水母 , 所有這些東西都存在 , 卡塔娜•莫塔說:是時候和它一起玩 。 摩托車帶領我們到驚喜和酷的新材料上 , 並且建議我們要找出他們對實驗、錫克做實驗、玩樂的方式 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力 , 設計 , 科技 , 科技 ,
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧型材料來演奏 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有個朋友 , 他的祖父從腳踏車和洗衣機中打造了一台車 , 讓他可以運輸他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起一輛車 , 也因為他知道怎麼建造 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾有一段時間 , 我們明白事情是如何運作的 , 了解它們是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何運作的 , 這樣我們就能建造、修復它們 , 或至少能對購買什麼做出明確的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀的第二半期間 , 許多自行行業的做法都消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創作者和開放原始碼的模型將這類知識帶入我們的生活中 , 我相信 , 我們需要把它們帶到下一個層面 , 到組成的層面上 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由紙製成的 , 以及它們如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚奇、精彩的複合塑膠 , 會改變形狀、油漆 , 會導電、顏色會改變顏色和布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨水能讓我們繪製電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上的這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來製造一個觸控感測器 , 用這個小小的光打開我的皮膚 , 會對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家使用導電墨水 , 但最近的發展指出 , 我們很快就會在雷射印表機和筆上使用 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這張紙上有無色光散佈的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 雖然一般的水晶只會在邊緣散射光線 , 這個光會在我打開周圍的光線時 , 整個表面都會亮光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料的兩種應用 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	溫度的溫度會改變溫度顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱板上 , 這個板子的溫度只比環境高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的原則之一 , 就是在嬰兒瓶裡 , 嬰兒瓶裡 , 它會指出 , 當內容物夠酷喝的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般一般所知的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會出現在我們日常使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車科幻小說告訴我們 , 但是我們可以有顏色的牆 , 根據溫度 , 鍵盤滾動 , 窗戶變成了開關的閃光 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 透過訓練 , 今天為什麼我要來這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何構成的 , 同時也因為我相信我們應該更深入地了解組成我們世界的成分 , 現在 , 我們對這些高科技合成的 , 我們的未來不會有足夠的了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在小量中取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何資訊可以用在如何使用它們 , 很少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 三年前 , 柯斯蒂男孩和我成立了一個專案 , 我們稱之為 「 開放式材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是一個網站 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 共享實驗、出版資訊 , 鼓勵大家隨時都能做出貢獻 , 和聚集資源 , 如研究報告和課輔 , 像我們這樣的人 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體的資料庫 , 資料庫 , 資料庫是智慧材料的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要關心智慧材料是如何運作的 ? 和它們是怎麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造出我們不了解的事物 , 和我們不了解的事物 , 最終 , 塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿著的衣服、房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是由tinker所推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家 , 從山腳踏車到半導體 , 個人電腦 , 飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學複雜且需要昂貴的設備
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學的兩位科學家在伊利諾州大學了解這一點 , 當他們發表了一篇文章 , 用比較簡單的方式製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他對化學物質和化學的體驗 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中繁殖 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至製作出他自己的蒸氣混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/maker的導師 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬丹接著在網路上發表了他的結果 , 包括他嘗試過的所有東西 , 卻沒有用 , 所以其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬丹的主要創新形式是 , 把一個實驗用在一個安裝的實驗室裡 , 設計在芝加哥的車庫裡 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 自己製作自己 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以找到他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程 , 改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提一下她的專案計畫的目的 , 是要強調材料的表現特質 , 同時專注在建造者的創造力和技巧上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置非常強大 , 它們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但在設計中 , 限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是模擬一系列的技術 , 來創造出非比尋常的物品 , 來讓我們免於預設的限制 , 來教導我們材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	我們在這裡看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 和mp3球員和磁鐵連接在一起 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜創建了一系列的紙講者 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電的布料和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他的製造家漢娜發表了她的配方 , 讓任何人複製和複製 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子產品是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 能讓我們製造更便宜和靈活的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝作品 , 她共享了她的發現 , 把門打開到一系列新的可能性 , 這兩者都在美學上吸引和創新 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 創作者有趣的是 , 我們創造出了熱情和好奇心 , 我們不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們通常會用非傳統的角度來處理問題 , 在這個過程中 , 最後會發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越來越多人在實驗材料 , 研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造他們的知識 , 更好的機會 , 創造出真正適合我們所有人的技術 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得tednelson在1970年代初 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須要了解電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些巨大的主題科學家 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人想過要在家裡做 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 關於新興科技的知識是最好的方法 , 以確保我們未來能有所說的話 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡泡 , 鎖住門 , 壓住加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛 , 引導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面的車子後面的幾輛 。 但如果車子能與他人分享資料 , 關於他們的位置和速度 , 並且用預測性模型來計算所有人在路上最安全的路線 , 珍妮•亨利會想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•赫利:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能會被避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但事實上 , 宗教的標誌和好運的魅力出現在世界各地的背叛中 , 我們知道這個事實是真實的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國十六歲到十九歲的主要死因 , 導致死亡 , 百分之七十五的意外和毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定的說法 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是高速公路上的年輕駕駛 , 前面的車子 , 我看到了煞車燈 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這個傢伙並沒有放慢 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停車 , 停車 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只需要65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我撞上了煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感到abs踢進去 , 車子還沒停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空袋子部署 , 車子已經被完全安裝了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道那輛車正在停車 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想我們可以轉換開車的經驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓各位思考一下駕駛的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 , 關上門 , 你在玻璃泡沫裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是要在半徑的路面上航行 , 和其他金屬巨人之間 , 在超人的速度下航行 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指引你兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你們所有的眼睛 , 不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但接著人們請你做這樣的事 , 你想要做出改變 , 第一件他們要求你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要去看你要去哪 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後在路上開車 , 看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 , 這是安全的開車方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做一個選擇 , 看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一件很棒的工作 , 選擇我們在路上的目的 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾 , 我們會感覺到不對或太晚了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數次意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看得太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但這項技術的存在 , 可以協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 隨著車子彼此交換資料 , 我們將能夠看到 , 不只是三台車在後面 , 三台車在左邊 , 全部都在同一時間 , 鳥的眼睛 , 我們將能夠看到這些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前面的汽車的速度 , 看看那傢伙的速度有多快 , 或是停車 。
