you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽買了一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿她的iphone , 放到機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給祖母 , 她住在這個國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她孫女一起玩躲藏的遊戲 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 當她可能只能看到她的孫女一年一次或一年兩次時 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這就是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在做的事 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 在一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google開放的架構上 , 叫做布洛克 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖著這些連續程式碼的積木 , 創造出任何你想要的機器人行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫程式來為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以模擬瀏覽器的行為 , 也就是左邊的romo在做的 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 並在現實生活中執行 , 執行這個計畫 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你感到自豪的話 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wi-fi的機器人都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以專注於建造一個人人都可以訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為個人機器人中最引人入勝的用途是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人和人之間的改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你在家裡有機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但是我們確實知道 , 這不是10年或100億美元 , 或大型人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 例如romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及讓你所有的機器人 , 我們等不及看到你建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進分子會討論女性、創造力、女性主義的定義當然 , 在這場演說中 , 熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球議題 , 愛 , 養育 , 說故事 , 女人 , 世界文化 , 世界文化 , 世界的文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝•阿言德說出了關於熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝各位 。 非常可怕 , 在這裡是聰明最聰明的人 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真的 ? 答案是:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 , 我想要傳達一個比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些讓我不安 , 直到我最後寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到周遭的神秘 , 所以我寫了有關巧合、教義、情感、夢想、自然的力量、魔法的力量 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我發表了幾本書但我在2006年2月時 , 直到2006年2月 , 當時我在義大利的冬季奧運會帶著奧運旗
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在人們在macy的作品中認識我 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我來談談我對名氣的四分鐘 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克典禮的組織者之一 , 開幕式的儀式 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟的其中一位 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答了 , 這肯定是錯誤的身分認同 , 因為我可以從運動員的角度來看 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以在沒有步行器的情況下走遍體育場 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧林匹克旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼衣服 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個制服 , 她說 , 要求我的測量值 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有了很大的遠景 , 像米開林男子一樣 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月的時候 , 我在土耳其發現自己熱切的群眾在街上任何八十個奧運團隊都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了遊戲中的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得勝利 , 但有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 一英吋的冰 , 風力的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有一個無懼且堅定的心會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道上有紅色海報宣布奧林匹克的口號
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活在這裡 , 不是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心就是驅使我們 , 決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要馬夫利克、異議人士、冒險家、外人和叛軍 , 他們會問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座的各位一樣 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	那些有常識的人 , 並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只能做出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間 , 我遇見了其他旗幟的熊:三位運動員 , 和女演員蘇珊•薩蘭登和蘇菲雅.羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 兩位有熱情心的女士:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞諾貝爾獎得主 , 他種了三千萬棵樹 。 藉此 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然 , 在許多村莊裡 , 經濟狀況也改變了 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	柬埔寨活動家索馬利馬 , 他對兒童賣淫有熱情的抗爭 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給兄弟 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男生強暴 , 她們相信和小時候的性行為 , 會從愛滋病中治癒她們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩子們每天被迫接收5、15個客戶 , 如果他們反叛 , 他們會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到了制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種衣服 , 但它離我預期的michelilinsuit很遠 , 不是真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	除了索菲亞•羅倫 , 大部份的國旗代表代表美與熱情 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲亞超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很迷人、很薄、很高 , 帶著很深的坦承 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深度的坦承 , 且沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視面試時 , 問: 「 她要如何看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直的 , 我沒有讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有塗鴉 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有小麥 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有距離 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚去體育場的翅膀 , 大聲說出奧運旗幟 , 順道一提 , 音樂的起始點 , 阿迪達大遊行的音樂 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲亞洛倫就在我面前 , 她比我高了一英尺 , 不算流行的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她很優雅地行走 , 就像在非洲薩凡納的長頸鹿 , 她肩上拿著旗子 。 我在我的觸角背後開著旗子 , 手臂上掛著旗子 , 所以 , 我的頭其實是在該死的旗子底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的攝影機 , 當然 , 在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的印刷照片中 , 我也出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都喜歡的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我人生中最棒的四分鐘是奧林匹克學院裡的那些人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我的丈夫在我說這句話時就被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋說我們在私人身上所做的事通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自接受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的媒體點擊這四分鐘 , 因為我不想忘記老年人摧毀我的大腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠帶著奧運熱情的關鍵字眼 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	1998年 , 那個地方是剛果的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所 , 都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡營 , 因為那些沒有殺害的人 , 會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 羅塞•圖爾多 , 她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她在丈夫受到折磨和殺害時看著她 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她讓七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生了雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用一根棍子剪下了木頭 , 用自己的頭髮來連結它 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她在營地指揮官的名字之後命名雙胞胎 , 用黑色茶餵食 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房裡爆發 , 強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓著她 , 拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著一把槍 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 運氣不凡 , 美國年輕人的熱情 , 薩夏•查諾夫 , 他成功把她放進美國救援機 , 羅倫•地圖 , 她的九個孩子 , 最後到亞利桑納州 , 在那裡 , 居住和茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖 , 在斯瓦希利 , 意思是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是強壯且熱情的女性 , 例如羅塞地圖 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編這些 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看到它們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代時期 , 在世界末端 , 在父權天主教和保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在我五歲的時候 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒到智利 , 所以沒人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 為了我的自由付出了很高的代價 , 並質疑父權 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能支付這筆錢 , 因為每次我收到的炸彈 , 我都能送兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 我女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說 , 女權主義是被約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場難忘的鬥爭 , 女權主義是被約會的 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒一樣有特權的女性 , 今天在座的各位 , 世界上大部分的姐妹 , 她們都被迫結婚 , 賣淫 , 被迫有勞工 , 她們不想要 , 或她們無法餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制身體或生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時被懲罰所殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	現今大部分的西方年輕女性 , 被稱為女權主義者是侮辱者 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也因缺乏男性而受苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死去 , 沒有任何意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個術語 , 改變它 , 為了女神的樣子 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為aphrodite , 或金星 , 或bimbo , 或任何你想要的 , 名字都不重要 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	在孟加拉村子裡 , 一個小小的婦女診所 。
the year is 2005 .	2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的牙醫衛 , 她在三週假期間 , 去了診所 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她已經準備好清潔牙齒了 , 但當她到達時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的獵物 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一系列的女性已經等了好幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在痛苦中 , 因為她有好幾顆腐爛的太陽能 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道 , 唯一的解決方案就是拉出壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒著很多的風險 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些噪音 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有個勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她謀殺了祈禱者 , 和手術一起前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生學家抽出更多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人在等她丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像個水馬遜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫脹到你看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫、憤怒、威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到害怕 , 但之後翻譯解釋了病人的狀況和手術沒有什麼關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打了她 , 因為她不在家準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上三分之二的女性勞動力 , 她們擁有不到1%的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水低於男性的薪水 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 而且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予女性教育、工作 , 控制她們自己的收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦權 , 她的孩子和她的家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮者 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的一個村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女性談話 , 解釋說 , 土地是荒謬的 , 因為他們砍掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女性種植新的樹木和水 , 掉下去 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五或六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村莊被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮、最後退的社會總是那些把女性放下來的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個明顯的真相卻被政府所忽略 , 還有慈善事業所忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊錢給女性的計畫 , 每一塊錢都有20美元給男性的計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔51%的人類 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量 , 會改變一切 , 不僅僅是科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向你們保證 , 女性一起工作 , 連結、有資訊、受教育 , 能將和平和繁榮帶到這個被破壞的星球上 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡都是平民百姓 , 主要是女性和孩童 。 他們是嚴重的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營這個世界 , 看著我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 以及人生的品質 , 為每個人充斥 , 不只為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月 , 我在柏克萊圖書館看到費南多布特羅的畫作 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊外 , 帶著博特羅的作品 , 卻勇於展示這幅畫 , 因為這個主題是阿布加拉伯的監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 在大量的鮑特羅風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法把這些影像從我的腦海或心中拿出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是不受懲罰的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 和濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 迫使其他群體接受現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都改變 , 但他們總是受惠 , 在這個例子中 , 棘手的效應 , 不適用在經濟上 , 完美地有效 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從梯子的頂部到底部的虐待技巧 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 特別是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最低潮的男人 , 也有可能會虐待一個女人或一個孩子的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了一些力量 , 透過性別、收入、種族 , 和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 此時此時此刻 , 要改變我們的文明 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的能源來管理這個世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一個關鍵的女性在權力的位置上 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能源 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是沒有希望的 , 我們得要等他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很想有蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但如果有了選擇 , 我寧願有威加里馬塔伊戰士的心臟 , 瑪麗 , 珍妮 , 羅斯地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它變得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼呢 ? 它是可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的知識 , 能源 , 天賦和技術 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫離我們的瘋狂 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦大小的城市裡 , 三千萬美金的大小上都要用 。 但是 , 所有的食物從哪裡來 ? 建築師的鋼鐵討論了每天餵養一個城市的日常奇蹟 , 展示了古老的食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 , 和城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	木材鋼鐵:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一座城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但它卻很少被問 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們去一間商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一小時內進入這間劇院的霧器 , 會在那裡等待我們 , 神奇地來自某處 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每天都有像倫敦一樣大的城市 , 足夠的食物必須被製造、運輸、買、買、賣、吃東西、被丟棄的城市 , 同樣的事每天都要發生在地球上的每個城市 , 都很了不起 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在像這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的事物 , 因為我們是動物 , 而我們需要吃的 , 我們其實是依賴大自然的 , 依賴我們的祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多的自然世界被轉化成非凡的景觀 , 像在我身後的那一片大豆田 , 位在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 以便餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些都是非凡的景觀 , 但我們當中有少數人能看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多的地景也不只餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人在吃肉 , 所以全球每年有三分之一的農作物被餵食給動物 , 而不是我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於這需要三倍的穀物 , 實際上是十倍的穀物來餵飽人類 , 如果是先通過動物的話 , 那不是很有效率的餵飽我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個更加嚴重的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 據估計 , 我們所居住的城市數量會是兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳酪的消耗量會增加兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市化的手在上升 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 飢餓的食肉動物餵飽食物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個很大的問題 。 實際上 , 如果我們把問題當作一個問題 , 我們就無法解決了 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有9千萬公頃的熱帶雨林都消失了 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了相當多的既有的artables , 來鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	每一卡路里需要10卡路里來生產西方每一卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然我們所生產的食物成本很高 , 但我們卻不太重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國一半的食物正在被丟棄 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	最後 , 在這段漫長的過程結束時 , 我們甚至無法妥善地餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人肥胖了 , 另外十億人挨餓了 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 全球80%的食物貿易只受控制只有5%的跨國企業控制 , 這張照片很可怕 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也在擁抱西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們是怎麼做到的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 先回答一個簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這個過程在古老的東部 , 稱為 「 肥沃 」 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	這也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 這兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化的發明 , 大約在同一時間 , 發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市都團結在一起 , 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為我們古老的祖先第一次發現了穀物來源 , 製造出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久定居處 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些居住地是什麼樣子 , 我們會發現它們是密切的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產出來的農場所包圍 , 由大型寺廟之類的主導 , 像是烏爾的這個 , 其實是精神化的 , 中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿組織了收割 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 把穀物送給神 , 接著提供了穀物 , 讓神不吃回人的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 這些城市的靈性和實體生活 , 都是由這些穀物所支配的 , 以及維持它們的收穫所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	當然 , 並非全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的是 , 羅馬在第一世紀 , 公民擁有約一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼形成的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古老的食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接近海洋 , 讓它可以從很遙遠的路上進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界 , 唯一可以做到的辦法 , 因為要把食物運送到馬路上是非常困難的 , 粗糙的 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	顯然 , 食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬在像汽車和埃及之類的地方 , 有效地發動戰爭 , 只為了取得他們的穀物儲備物 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的是一大堆 , 漫長的 , 軍事化的購物中心 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到:羅馬曾經從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在一個階段 , 我認為那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬用它的胃口塑造了它的印度地 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 工業界還有另一件事也發生了 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看倫敦在十七世紀的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它是從thames , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們的道路到便宜的成本 , 主要的市場也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看這些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你就可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 對魚來說也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是靠河流進來的 。 同樣的事 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比爾辛格更有名的是倫敦的魚市場直到1980年代中期
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的很不尋常 , 仔細想想 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都在附近遊蕩 , 帶著行動電話 , 看起來像磚頭 , 有點像在港口的魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	城市裡的食物是另外一件事:一旦它的根部進入城市 , 它們就很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是個非常不同的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以 , 倫敦的肉大部分來自西北、蘇格蘭、威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 它就進來了 , 到達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 被放在那兒 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	波爾特利從東北部來到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女人在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥兒會用腳來保護腳的鞋 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	接著 , 當它們撞到便宜的東邊時 , 就會被賣掉 , 這就是為什麼稱為 「 文化 」 的原因 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看工業時代之前的任何一座城市地圖 , 你就可以追蹤食物來到它那裡 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 不論是閱讀街道的名字 , 都能給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前的生活中 , 星期五 , 你去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密菲爾德的影像 , 你可以看到 , 要住在這樣的城市 , 要知道你的食物從何而來 , 很難過 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在星期日午餐時 , 機會是它在你的窗外流血 , 大約三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年偉大西方國家的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視覺和心智中被屠殺 , 在鄉下某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們來到城裡 , 鐵軌上 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首先 , 這讓城市能夠生長 , 大小和形狀 , 在任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市被地理限制了 ; 過去 , 他們必須透過非常困難的實體方式來取得他們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們從地理位置中得到了有效的解放 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所見 , 從倫敦的地圖上看到的 , 在火車出現的90年後 , 它是從一個很容易被動物吃進來的小球 , 以此類推 , 到一個很大的球體 , 那會是非常非常、非常困難的 , 要不就是對任何人 , 不論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然那只是開端 , 火車來了之後 , 火車來了 , 在這過程的最後 , 這塊標示了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市最後的解放 , 從任何與大自然的關係中解放出來 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種沒有聞到味道的城市 , 沒有混亂的城市 , 肯定沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們把食物帶到車上 , 開車到外面的一個盒子裡 , 帶著一週的購物回來 , 想知道在地球上有什麼用途 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們的關係 , 與食物和城市之間的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有食物 , 以前是市中心 , 市中心的社交核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它以前是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 只要加水 , 或加一點點蛋 , 只要你做蛋糕或其他東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是讀了一包包包裝的後面標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不重視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評價它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統的諷刺之一 , 就是它們已經讓它們承諾要變得更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	若要在任何地方及任何地方建立城市 , 都能真正讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	他們也讓我們依賴體制 , 只能提供 , 如同我們所見 , 他們的體制是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪士多問自己什麼 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的最前線 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉 , 一個人基本上都是農業的 , 在後園裡種植蔬菜 , 一起吃共產的餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的基本秩序原則 , 儘管你從來沒有把它弄成那樣 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個很有名的 「 烏托邦 」 的願景 , 伊貝茲霍華 , 《花園城》 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半獨立城市 , 一小塊大都市的東西 , 附近的土地圍繞著鐵路 , 彼此連結 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他的願景的秩序原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但和霍華德的這個願景毫無關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是烏托邦想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是thomasmoore刻意使用的一個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以意味著一個好的地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 它是幻想的 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類dwell的深層問題 , 這樣就不太用了 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 西托邦 , 來自古希臘文 , 「 食物 」 和 「 湯 」 的地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經生活在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到 , 我們可以把食物當作一個強大的工具 , 一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 來塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 蘇托邦看起來會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 只是狗臉上的樣子 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是人生中央的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 享受著時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是我們社會的糧食 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但除非你有像這樣的人 , 否則你就不能有這樣的場景 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順道一提 , 這些也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	那些思考食物的人 , 想想前面的食物 , 他們計畫 , 可以盯著一堆原料蔬菜 , 並且認得出這些食物 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網絡的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些類型的人 , 我們就沒有這種地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這個 , 因為這是一個買蔬菜的男人 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡 , 市場 , 當地的食物正在成長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	它很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	這是城市社交生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為如果沒有這些 , 你就不能有這種地方 , 當地的食物種植 , 同時也是地景的一部分 , 而不只是一個零和的商品 , 在一些未被發現的海洛威 ,
cows with a view .	牛的視角是 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆的 「 嗡 」 。
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西整合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪過的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們會告訴所有有關食物的議題 , 並且種植他們自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫凱文的植物 , 或許是屬於一個叫凱文的孩子的植物 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這種試圖和大自然重新連結的計畫是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到 , 西托邦已經存在於各地的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於把它們加入 , 用食物當作一種看待方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就會停止將城市視為大城市 , 大都市 , 沒有生產力的爆炸 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免連接的一部分 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的影像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入考慮永續發展 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張影像總結了我認為我們應該要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是一個重新概念化的食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是來自650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	它是安布羅吉歐.羅倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉村之間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在我要我們問 , 如果他今天畫出這張圖 , 阿布羅吉歐.羅倫澤蒂會怎樣 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天的好政府會長什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們是吃什麼的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解到 , 世界也是我們吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以把食物當作強大的工具 , 來塑造世界變得更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	來自慈悲的章節 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀時看到宗教的角色:它會讓我們分裂嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們團結在一起嗎 ? 她會檢討世界上的信仰 , 來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarenarmstrong:咱們回顧黃金法則:咱們重新審視黃金法則:
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我感到很挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我很敏銳地意識到在世界各大宗教信仰中 , 同情心的中心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都演化了他們自己的 「 黃金法則 」 的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它出現在一個正面的版本中 , 「 永遠對待別人 , 只要你想要被對待自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面版本的 「 不要對別人做你不喜歡的事 」 。
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現你痛苦的是什麼 , 然後拒絕任何情況下的痛苦 , 去衝突別人的痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很棒 , 也因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施金融規則時 , 如混亂所說的: 「 一整天 , 日復一日 」 , 不只是做好你做好的事 , 還要回到貪婪和自尊的人生 , 每天都要做 , 每天 , 要從你的世界的中心 , 把自己丟到另一個地方 , 然後你超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它帶你進入了被稱為 「 神 」 的存在 , nirvana , rama , tao 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們在自我意識中所知的事物 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道 , 這對宗教生活來說是很重要的 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有了一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚在一起時 , 他們會爭論的是abstrustrustrines , 或說出仇恨的會議 , 或對同性戀或類似的情況 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常 , 人們並不想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我和一群宗教人士交談時 , 會有一種互相交流的表情 , 因為人們通常會想做對的對話 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	當然這也打敗了運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我如此感謝ted呢 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書本研究帶我到21世紀 , 讓我可以和更多的觀眾說話 , 比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不把黃金法則用在全球 , 這樣我們就對待所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們是誰 , 都跟我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來協助下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的偉大任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 如我所說的 , 在那裡 , 人們可以住在和平中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為是問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種想像的同理心行為 , 讓自己處在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有選擇 , 對我來說 ,
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以說出去 , 或是強調我們的信仰的教條 , 或包容的面向 , 或我們可以回到拉比希爾 。 拉比•希爾爾 , 老舊的耶穌當代 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 被問到整個猶太教條時 , 他說: 「 這對你來說是仇恨的 , 不要對你的鄰居做事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這是托拉和其他的一切 , 只有評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂的早期父親和拉比人說 , 任何對經文的詮釋都不合理 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們得要復甦這個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	不只是因為愛情的靈魂把我們吞下去 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們得要讓這一切發生 , 且我們能用ted介紹的現代通訊做這件事 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的回應感到非常的心碎 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人會用charter來療癒 , 最近他們在新加坡社會中被打擾 , 有些國會的成員想要用政治的方式實踐它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一項藝術展覽 , 引領藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們看到 , 同情心也在所有藝術的根源上 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區都在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論在伊斯蘭和所有信仰中 , 同情心的中心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停止在那裡 , 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教學讓我們錯了 , 專注於相信抽象教義的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學必須永遠引起行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在我死去的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續我們的合作夥伴來做兩件事 , 教育和刺激同情心 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經失去同情心了 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這意味著對某人感到抱歉
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	當然 , 如果你想一想 , 你就不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體在協助解決一些我們對他人的刻板印象時的刻板印象 , 把我們從別人身上分開來 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我想讓年輕人了解動態、動態和同情生活方式的挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	還可以看到 , 它需要急性智能 , 不僅僅是奇怪的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己的同情心主題 , 以及其他人的傳統 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵對於不親切的言論的敏感度 , 所以 , 因為人們有這個章節 , 不論他們的信念或缺少什麼 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰不相同的言論 , 不論他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖 , 或行業的首位 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過把章節放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然困在古老世界裡 , 一個大堆的棺材 , 坐在房間裡 , 再進行另一個阿卡尼語的陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹了我一個全新的思維方式 , 和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted的美好之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有的專業知識 , 如果我們一起參與 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎很棘手 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一句話 , 結束英國作者的評論 , 一位牛津作家 , 我不太常引用c.lewis 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事 , 自從我讀書的時候 , 一直以來 , 一直以來 ,
it's in his book " the four loves . "	他的書《四個愛》 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他在愛情中分辨出愛情 , 當兩個人凝視 , 彈珠 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在同一邊 , 肩膀肩膀肩膀 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上對方 , 但我們也可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我感到非常強烈 , 在維尼的小活動中 , 當所有不同的說服者聚集在一起時 , 站在同一方的目標上 , 兩者之間的差異會融化 。
and we learn amity .	我們學到了野心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會一起生活 , 學會彼此認識 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmcaulay反映了風力和有時很神奇的旅程 , 朝著羅馬帝國的競爭 , 他對歷史的城市展現出了敬意 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgarthur , 藝術 , 藝術 , 書籍 , 城市 , 溝通 , 文化 , 設計 , 娛樂 , 幽默 , 說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫得更好 , 懂東西 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時我畫了很多圖 , 我仍然不知道我在畫什麼 。
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	那些對數位東西感到舒服的人 , 甚至對那段關係感到很不舒服 , 想知道 , 最有名的 「 工作方式 」 的人 , 同時 , 為了了解 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試著讓他的筆記型電腦和他的新cdburner溝通 。
who knew about extension managers ?	誰知道延伸經理 ?
i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直都管理自己的延伸 , 這樣我就沒想到要讀這些指令 , 但我終於明白了 。 我終於明白了 。 因為 , 邀請來到這裡 , 聲稱沒有投影機 , 所以 , 把這些卡爾帶到不再是必要的 , 另一種溝通形式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我所熟知的事物 , 特別適合許多技術性思維的人 , 或我可以談論我真正關心的事物 。

now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	我為什麼要關心羅馬 , 尤其是 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在六零年代 , 參加了羅德島設計學院 , 研究建築 。
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 去年我五歲的時候 , 在羅馬當學生 , 改變了我的人生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	並不是最不理由 , 過去四年 , 我曾在家裡住過 , 開車到瑞士 , 開車回家 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了1960年代 。 我讀到他們 , 我知道他們很有趣 。 我錯過了他們 , 但是我在羅馬度過了不凡的一年 , 這是我從未想過的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 每當有機會時 , 我都會試著在裡面做點什麼 , 或用它來做 。

things that i want them to believe i understand .	我希望他們相信我理解的事物 。

there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	這裡有一條非常薄的藍色路線 , 讓它穿過這個東西 , 可以把它們整合在一起 。

a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不只是收集和儲存資訊的方式 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層從另一層剝下來 ; 我們認為他們是頁面 , 用一定的方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是層層層層的地層 , 垂直層次 , 我想 , 只要把頁面撕下來 , 就會允許我用正確的方式去思考 , 讓我來看看深層層層的地層 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築的牆面上 , 包含了疤痕 ; 數世紀以來 , 改變的疤痕經過這些結構 , 而不是被撕碎 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你解開它 , 你可以看到它背後的 「 疤痕組織 」 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 讓小窗戶變得很重要 , 因為壞人來了 , 等等 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	所有的適應都被埋在黏土下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這個palazzo的頁面向你們展示它內部的狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但更重要的是 , 我也能向你們展示它的樣子 , 在那些巨大的石頭積木的角落 , 或用磚塊和木頭做成的假石塊 , 通常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點三維 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你帶走一條狹窄的小路 , 到那些令人驚訝的小範圍中 , 用雙邊摺疊網頁 , 如果你像我一樣 , 讀一本小時候的頁面 , 希望你能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你在你腦海周圍的頁面 , 在那短暫的一段時間內 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我真的沒有做過比摺疊頁更複雜的東西 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我又想 , 也許我可以在這裡簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	咱們來看看萬神廟 , 以及前面的廣播廣播廣場 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開這本書 , 如果我打開它90度 , 我們就在看萬神廟的前方 , 我們就在看上方 , 往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我用另一種方式翻書 , 我們會在萬神廟的前方看到廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺紙 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本書 , 沒有完整的開口 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我心想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 我甚至可以把摺紙和唯一的部分打開的書結合在一起 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入萬神廟 , 它會不斷成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我站在正確的軌道上 , 但它失去了它的人類特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓大家注意書 , 一路收集資訊 , 總是一件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 把我當成一個抓住的標題 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果它是一只熱情的鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奇怪 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那段旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題運作 , 用它 , 那會是一趟旅程 , 穿越羅馬 , 展示了我喜歡羅馬的東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是一隻鴿子坐在教堂上 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天離開 , 做正常的鴿子 , 回來 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網子覆蓋 , 這種鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它會需要找到另一個居住的地方 , 這讓我可以通過我最愛的目錄 , 我們從高高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人住在一起 , 這不一定是件好事 , 但它確實可以再次把鴿子帶回來 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了這個老傢伙 , 照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 讓他們有危險的地方 , 什麼不了 , 他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學著為他做個技巧 , 在午餐時間 , 娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在老人和這些鴿子之間 , 有一個真實的連結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事的尾端感到非常生病 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教導他們拼他的名字 , 阿爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天後出現 , 沒有看到他 , 他住在這個小垃圾桶裡 , 拼了他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到了足夠的力量 , 把梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘記要提到:每當他失去了鴿子時 , 他就會把這隻鴿子帶到城市的牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬古老的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有在牆壁中埋藏過 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很愉快的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長一段路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	所以 , 總之 , 我經歷了...... , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒有去任何地方 , 我就想出了頭銜 , 希望這個頭銜會把我踢出正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它會讓我專注在我身上 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁面 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題頁面 , 最終引導我去解決我安定的解決方案 , 一個年輕女子的故事 , 一個她在羅馬城外圍的住宅鴿子上傳訊息給城市中的某人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	鴿子在飛行的上方飛越亞伯利亞 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松果等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅色線 , 你會看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅色的線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得必要且有可能 , 嘗試傳達出飛越城市的感覺 , 而不動的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	越過了凱索的金字塔 , 看來你會很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒有去羅馬渡河過大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的事 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這種鴿子會做一些事情 , 大部分的居住鴿子不會做的事情:它需要一個可怕的路線 , 我覺得它是必要的裝置 , 可以把這本書延伸到四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們在哥倫比亞的哥倫比亞圍繞著哥倫比亞的哥倫比亞教堂 , 和海克力士的神殿 , 朝向河邊 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和米開朗基羅所設計的palazofarzofarzofarnese所設計出來的石頭 , 建造的石頭 , 來自哥倫比的狹隘逃離 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們沿著camampodefiori下潛 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為它是一個完整的戰場化 , 否認任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的規則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出這些消失點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 一對在蒙蒙尼亞 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖地亞馬利亞的前面 , 在那裏 , 足球賽正在進行 , 我們被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是個很糟糕的例子 , 被足球擊中 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的碎片:有聖塔•黛拉•維爾 , 有一顆足球 , 有一隻鳥的翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我得要重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖塔•德拉•德拉斯的步調 , 這些書很有彈性 , 非常有互動性 , 只要把它轉過來 , 再看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅線所捕捉到的影響 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類會把自己拉過來 , 穿過中世紀的高塔 , 只有少數幾個中世紀的高塔 , 前往聖塔的教堂上 , 周圍的圓頂向下 , 向下看 , 看了幾次 , 看到了 , 飛過了幾次 ; 還有伯尼的雕像 , 穿過了四條河的美麗的布羅米諾的聖人 , 停止了足夠長的時間 , 停止在我們呼吸的第26英尺長的松樹上 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們可以在裡面、四處走動 , 因為我們在飛翔 , 我們不用擔心重力 , 在這個特定的時刻 , 所以這幅圖可以用任何方式在頁面上 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們經過gesu時 , 我們會有點開心 , 這樣並不會模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	在我剛提到的美麗的牆壁上 , 裝滿了我剛才所提到的合成物 ; 美麗的雕刻在尼龍 「 崛起 」 標誌上方的牆壁之上 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們到達了帕拉扎索的庭院 , 這是我們的目的 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一個小窗戶 , 進入了畫板 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把這個訊息從鳥的腿上移除 , 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的事 , 事實上 , 鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程 , 紅線延伸了所有的視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 我們完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只要讀一下這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的天際研究員skylartebbits在自我組裝上工作 , 不如建造東西 , 我們可以創造出自己 , 多麼像dnazip一樣的材料 。 這是在初期 , 一個很大的概念 ; tibbit向我們展示了三個伊斯拉伯的計畫 , 展現出一個自我組裝的未來 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylarlarlartititits:我們能做出自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向各位展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自我組裝、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向各位展示我相信的 , 是目前製造業的狀態 , 然後將它和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓 , 兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的新技術 , 鋼筋、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器 , 能帶我們進入太空五年──[組裝的時間]250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看看自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以摺疊成一萬奈秒 , 或三十億鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製出大約三十億鹼基對 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的天然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 比起任何東西 , 都還要有效率 , 遠遠超過我們所能建造的任何複雜度 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以修復自己的壽命 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天然系統有一點很有趣 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將它翻譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的實體環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼我們想要建造的東西的複雜度 , 讓建築物和機器變得更複雜 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編寫的零件 , 可以用這些序列來摺疊 , 或重新組合 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源 , 讓它能啟動 , 讓我們的零件能夠從這個計畫中折疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些錯誤的修正措施 , 以確保我們成功地建造出我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看幾個項目 , 是我在麻省理工學院的同事和我正在努力完成這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先 , 巨型機器人和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些計畫是大規模的可重建機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入了機械裝置 , 感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你解碼你想要摺出來的東西 , 一連串的角度 , 非常負面的120 , 120 , 120 , 120 , 負面120 , 負面的120 , 像這樣 ; 一連串的角度 , 或轉向 , 然後把序列從弦中發送 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都帶著它的負120個訊息 , 轉到那邊 , 檢查一下 , 然後把它傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真的會帶來光明:這是真的可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美金 , 許多人小時來製造這個8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們能把機器人放到每一個部位嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動性大自然 , 或被動地試圖重新組合程式性 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它進一步進一步 , 它嘗試進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了電腦計算最基本的基礎基礎 , 數位邏輯門 , 直接嵌入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nand大門 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是門 , 它會做你的電腦運算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 就像你在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個是先前的磚塊 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	接著 , 它會給你3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思是 , 使用者可以開始加入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算著它以前所做的事 , 你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 向上或向下移動 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , 輸入等於0的輸出值 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入是1輸出的產量 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們所有的資訊都嵌入在他們身上 , 說明了什麼是建構出來的 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱之為 「 自體複製 」 , 因為你的結構包含了真實的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你就可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入來告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以有一些東西可以爬上去 , 讀到它 , 並且可以輸出一個到一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 , 沒有外部指示 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個專案 , 叫做 「 偏見鏈 」 , 它可能是我們現在最令人興奮的例子──被動的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上 , 你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都是完全相同的 , 且它們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一個鏈 , 或每個元素 , 都想要左轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該左轉或右轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖動鏈時 , 它會摺成任何你編寫過的裝置 , 在這個案例中 , 或這個案例中 , 兩個立方體相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上 , 你可以設計任何立體形狀 , 或單面形狀 , 兩維 , 完全被動地進入這個鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來的資訊 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的可能性 , 是我們的實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些部件中有新的可程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後你就有了新的計算能力 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的平行和分散的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這很令人興奮 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些計畫只是一個小步驟 , 要是我們實施這些新的自我組合世界的新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們已經在海底的兩次大陸上去了 。 下一代去探索了什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃夫斯建議了這個答案:幾乎所有事情 。 我們都可以開始 , 說 , 與聯合國世界的一致 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性 , 探索 , 微生物學 , 科學 , 科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼可以探索的 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一個二十世紀偉大的探險家 , 羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國自然歷史博物館 , 安德魯斯領導了一系列的探險 , 未經發現的地區 , 例如在戈比沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他說 , 他後來是印第安納瓊斯的角色 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛的貝洛特市 , 我給一群中學的學生公開演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演講時 , 比在ted演講還要嚇人一點 , 那就要試著注意一千十二歲的孩子 , 一個四十五分鐘的演講 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但在那之後 , 有一個問題一直困在我身上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 有很多人有一種感覺 , 地球上探索的偉大時代已經結束了 , 在下一代 , 他們得要去外太空 , 或最深的海洋 , 才能找到重要的東西去探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是事實嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們真的沒有什麼東西可以讓我們探索在地球上嗎 ?
