it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回到生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知的世界探險家 , 馬丁•貝吉尼克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的是從菸草植物中取出受感染的果汁 , 用較小的過濾器過濾過它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到了他認為外面一定有比當時所知最小型的細菌還小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀取了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在解開病毒時 , 貝傑金真的為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道 , 病毒組成了地球上大部分的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式的生命形式 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然 , 已經有很大的實用應用 , 和這個世界有關 , 像是根除天花 , 疫苗的出現 , 對抗子宮頸癌的出現 , 我們現在知道 , 大部分是由人類乳腺病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但是我們沒有意識到我們星球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些很棒的工具可以讓我們探索未知的世界 , 像是深度定序之類的 , 讓我們能做的不只是滑雪表面 , 看看特定物種的個別基因組 , 再看看全部的微生物群組 , 周圍和記錄這些物種中的所有基因資訊 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以把這些技巧應用在土壤、皮膚上 , 和中間的東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在定期地做這個實驗 , 來辨識出造成它們的爆發造成的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你了解這個方法是如何運作的 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上拿了一把鼻腔的腫脹 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常在尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 我們會看到許多常見的嫌犯 , 當然 , 很多人類的基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大多來自你鼻子內完全沒有傷害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常令人驚訝的現象 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始看這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子裡大約20%的基因信息 , 沒有任何植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們完全不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這類資料的小組 , 當中有一些人開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前所見到的 ; 它和我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸相似 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為 , 你的鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的資訊是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對比較不穩定的血液中 , 大約1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法被輸入或配對任何我們之前見過的資訊 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越精確 , 我們決定了這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少有些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 其實只是在嬰兒期間 , 有一個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:在這個生命中 , 被埋藏在這個基因信息中 , 代表著尚未被分辨出來的生命 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索a、t、c、g的弦時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命種類 , 例如beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學的本質的方式 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	或許可以讓我們找出一種癌症的成因 , 會衝突我們 , 或找出我們不熟悉的疾病來源 , 或可能創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能宣布 , 和史丹佛大學、加州理工學院和ucsf的同事一起 , 我們正在開始一項計畫 , 來探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新形式的生命存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 生命的形式 , 構成地球上大部分的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會很驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到一種全新的生活階級 , 其實就在我們鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	沒錯 , 我們可能已經繪製了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們也許已經發現了所有外面的哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈教訓給下一代的探險家提供了重要的一課 , 像是那位來自威斯康辛的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們說出這一課 , 就會像這樣:不要假設我們現在認為的就是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在你選擇去探索的領域之後 , 去探索暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊有未知的事物 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇的科學家大衛•德修斯把理論物理放在後面的燃料上 , 來討論更迫切的物質:人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、全球議題、物理、科學、宇宙、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在宇宙中的位置上 , 在我們的位置上 , 在宇宙中的大衛deutsch上 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知去肢體上 , 說些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我要從大家已經知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的記錄歷史已知 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其他地方 , 都是為了維持我們的進化或創造 , 如同以前所想的 , 以及我們現在的存在 , 最重要的是 , 未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的想法是 , 在太空船外 , 宇宙是不可避免的敵意 , 而內在是我們所擁有的 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 大家都知道的第二件事 , 與大多數人類歷史上所相信的相反 , 人類其實不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金所說的 , 我們只是一顆在典型的星球表面的化學氣體 , 繞著典型的恆星繞著軌道 , 在典型的銀河系的外面 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家所知道的這兩件事的第一件事 , 就是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 特別適合 , 第二件事就是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	特別是如果你把這兩種深刻的真相視為生存的深層真相 , 告訴你們你們的人生決策 , 那麼 , 他們似乎有點互相衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們完全錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	他們是 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個例子開始 , 典型的這個地方 , 是典型的嗎 ? 嗯 , 咱們來看看四周 , 看看隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學風景 , 完全不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要走幾百英里 , 往同一個方向看 , 回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆壁或化學風景 , 你看到的是一個藍色的星球 。 如果你進一步看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星在星系中出現 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河系外 , 回頭看 , 是的 , 有一個巨大的銀河系 , 上面有螺旋槳在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們已經從這裡來了十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們仍然沒有在宇宙中典型的地方附近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到一個典型的地方 , 就要到達一千倍的星系空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是怎麼樣的 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在龐大的代價下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 讓星系間的空間從星系空間來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 請看 , 看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太完美 , 你可以看到 , 在星際空間中間的空間中 , 完全是黑暗的 , 音高的暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	黑暗之處在於 , 如果你要看最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星要爆炸成超新星 , 你要直接盯著它看 , 當它的光照到你時 , 你仍然無法看見甚至是一顆閃亮的閃光燈 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙的大小和暗度 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管事實超新星如此亮 , 很聰明 , 它會殺死你數光年的石頭 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 到目前為止 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	在絕對零度之上 , 它也非常寒冷 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	它是空的 , 真空的 。 真空的密度比地球上最高的技術少了一百萬倍 , 目前所能創造出的高密度還要少 。 所以 , 一個典型的地方有多麼不同 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是不典型的地方 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈打開嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們如何知道一個遙遠的環境 , 如此不同 , 外星人 , 與我們以前習慣的環境有關 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球的環境 , 以我們所處的形式 , 創造出知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這意味著什麼 ? 嗯 , 看看外面比我們這裡所說的更遠一點 , 用望遠鏡 , 你會看到看起來像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 四分之一 」 , 原本的意思是 「 量子論 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著有些東西看起來像星星 , 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	數十億年前 , 我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億光年後 , 星系中心的材料崩塌在超大質量的黑洞中 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場引導了一些重力崩潰的能量 。 有些物質在巨大的噴射流中 , 以我認為的光輝為光輝的光輝中 , 產生了一兆陽光 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不可能和噴射機的物理更不一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在一瞬間就存活下來 。 當嘗試描述那些噴射機中 , 語言就斷裂了 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像在經歷超級新星爆炸 , 但在瞬間 , 數百萬年來 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射機在幾十億年後發生 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學風暴可以準確地描述、模型 , 並預測 , 最重要的是 , 你的參考結果 , 現實中發生了什麼事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個實體系統 , 大腦 , 包含了一個精確的工作模型 , 另一個區域 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	雖然它包含了這張圖像 , 但它也包含了這個解釋模型 , 體現出相同的數學關係和因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠精彩 , 信念和另一種結構相似 , 就是隨著時間的增加 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這種實體物體 , 與其它可能性不同 , 儘管它體現了相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越長 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是種化學氣體 , 不同 。 這種化學氣體有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著不斷增加的精準度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是在宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個中心 , 本身包含著整個物理世界的結構和因果的本質 。 到目前為止 , 物理世界的所有法則 , 都不被忽略了 , 事實上 , 物理的法律允許它 , 甚至使它發生 , 最重要的事情 , 就是物理世界的一個中心 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和環境的形式 , 在我們與宇宙的其他地方建立了這種特殊的關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 史蒂芬•霍金的remark是真的 , 但它是錯的 , 但它是錯誤的強調 。 一件事是對的 。 一件事是 , 它與任何特殊的物理無關 , 沒有奇蹟 , 只不過它有三樣東西 , 豐富 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的成長是一種資訊處理的形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要電腦 , 不用物質製造電腦 , 不需要有所謂的電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 要讓媒體在我們發現的知識上記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 比較不具體 , 但對於開放式的知識、解釋來說 , 最重要的是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	比方說 , 我們剛好要測試牛頓的重力定律 , 大約300年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但過去的證據顯示 , 地球上每一平方公尺深落在地球上 , 數十億年後 , 將會持續下降 , 數十億年後 , 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發現所有科學中最基本的真相 , 只是為了我們地球上取得的證據 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 也有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個前提是開放式的知識創造的前提是最低的可能供應量 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說的 , 它是空的 ; 它是冷的 ; 它是暗的 。 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系空間裡的立方體 , 和我們的家 , 太陽系一樣大 , 現在的立方體是非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	比方說 , 一座自制的太空站 , 有一群科學家致力於創造出一個開放式的知識流 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 除了科技之外 , 還要收集來自星系間空間的氫氣 , 再將它結合成其他元素 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個完整的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼能阻止我們去做 , 除非知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的問題 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動使用能源供給 , 因為交通運輸是核融合反應器和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再說一次 , 外頭是黑暗的 。 但是你只需要用望遠鏡 , 即使是現今的設計 , 外觀 , 你就會看到相同的銀河系 , 就像我們從這裡看到的一樣 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你會看到恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	或許最困難的科學會是生物學領域的實地考察 , 因為要花好幾億年才能到最近的生物體系 , 回到最近的地球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有像生物學領域的旅程那麼多 , 我想我們只要每幾億年就可以完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了所有公開的知識創造的前提 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙中 , 都可以成為我們一樣的中心 , 如果知識的存在 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並非處於一個獨一無二的友善的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎是所有環境 。 那麼地球就是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制性因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點我認為應該讓我們感到非常特別 。 但這也讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有必要的特定知識 , 我們就無法存活在宇宙中持續的挑戰中 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一顆超級新星 , 才能離開幾年之外 , 我們就會死去 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁.雷斯最近寫了一本關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性書 , 從天體物理、科學實驗 , 都出錯了 , 最重要的是 , 恐怖主義有大規模毀滅性的武器 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為 , 在這個世紀 , 文明只有50%的機率存活下來 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他接下來會在會議上談這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他這件事 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們也無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它不取決於機率 , 但不論我們是否在時間內創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不存在前所未有的物種隨時都滅絕
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數物種和所有的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為一個例外 , 那麼邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是利用一種特徵來區分我們的物種 , 和我們的文明 , 來自其他物種 , 我們的特殊關係 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 創造出新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 成為存在的擁抱 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要倡導任何特殊的解決方案 , 只是說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 在全球暖化方面 , 我只是個拉曼人 。 對一個拉曼來說 , 理性的事情是 , 嚴肅地說待科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太晚了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們目前最好的選項就是要預防二氧化碳排放 , 例如京都議定書 , 因為它對於經濟活動的限制 , 以及它的巨大成本 , 數百億美元之類的 , 那就已經是個災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被倡導的行為 , 甚至沒有被迫去解決這個問題 , 只是稍微的解答它 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 它可能已經太晚了 , 已經無法避免它了 , 自從任何人意識到危險之前 , 就已經太晚了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代時 , 可能已經太晚了 , 當最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放將要在未來的新年齡 , 數十億人會死去 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這教訓對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是說 , 我們永遠不知道 。 當我們知道一個即將發生的災害時 , 要如何解決它 , 比災難本身的成本還低 , 那就沒有太多的爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有預防的原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的一點 , 不僅僅是避免問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	沒錯 , 一連串的預防措施等同於一磅的療法 , 但只有在我們知道要預防什麼才行 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你在鼻子上被打斷了 , 那麼醫學的科學並不符合你如何避免干擾 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學界停止尋找治療的方法 , 只專注在預防上 , 那它也可能達到極少的成就 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此時此刻 , 世界正在發動計畫 , 用全部的成本來強制減少氣體排放量 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和計畫一起努力 , 要降低溫度 , 計畫要活在更高的溫度上 , 而不是全部成本 , 而是有效率地和便宜 。 有些計畫存在 , 像是在太空中 , 大量鏡子會把陽光反射 , 鼓勵水生態有機體來吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些東西正在進行快速研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類要面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般來說 ,
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 把正確的能力 , 不是無限避免的好運運 , 不是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 還有生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以 , 拿兩塊石板 , 雕刻在他們身上 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 卡維: 「 問題是唯一的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一方面 , 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果它被困在一個不好規則的體制中 , 一個掙扎的國家 , 如果它被困在一個貧窮的體制中 ? 經濟學家保羅默揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 章節城市 」 、 「 市區 」 , 被國家聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、經濟、全球議題、政治、商業、經濟、全球議題 , 政治、政治、政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅默的根本想法是:charter的城市城市 ,
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	這對我們來說是一個令人著迷的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有任何電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我也見過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色襯衫中的一個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:nelson 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以使用尖端技術 , 像手機一樣 , 但無法取得100歲的科技 , 讓家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	換言之 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新技術帶進來 , 讓它們變成像nelson這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的電力公司在一個規則之下運作 , 表示它必須以非常低、補助的價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 價格低於每單位銷售的單位 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 沒有獎勵 , 也沒有獎勵 , 來接納許多其他使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到有不同的規則可以有一套規則 , 規則讓企業賺一筆小利潤 , 所以他們有動機去簽更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是手機公司的規則 , nelson購買了他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以 , 他試著改變電價價格的規則 , 但從商業和消費者身上 , 試圖改變電力價格的規則 , 但卻是從商業和消費者身上取得的抗議行為 , 他們想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他困住了一些規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案來協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	nelson在街燈下讀書 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們能改變規則的方法 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們是否有一些規則可以發展來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個普遍的抽象概念 , 可以實踐 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予更多人選擇 , 在許多國家 , 更多的領導者選擇就是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但這兩者之間的反對度很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給予領導人的選擇 , 像給總統選項 , 讓總統在電力上提高價格 , 消除人們想要的經濟選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消費補助電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	如果你只給某一邊或另一邊 , 你會有緊張或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到方法 , 讓兩者都有更多選擇 , 那會給我們一套改變規則 , 來讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則損害的效應 , 規則可以讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是在亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在線上 , 和鄰居相比 , 黑洞就好像黑洞一樣 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會很訝異 , 北韓的規則會讓人們處在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 要知道北韓和南韓都從同樣的規則開始 , 以法律和法規的角度和法規的角度來看 , 但在更深層層的層面來看 , 了解、規範、文化、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了選擇 , 為他們的規則帶來了非常多樣的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們人類可以改變我們身為人類的規則 , 可以改變我們使用的規則 , 來彼此互動 , 為了更好 , 或更糟糕 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地的位置 , 在網路上 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 與其鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國 , 居民數目差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家與波多黎各都很黑暗 , 和波多明尼亞共和國有一半的居民 , 不論是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是規則不好 , 因為在北韓 , 政府太強壯 , 壓迫性 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造一個有好規則的環境 , 我們就不能只撕下它 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	在這個圖表的開端 , 中國是世界上的高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 像是鋼、印刷、槍枝 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在這段期間 , 有效的規則 , 鼓勵那些想法的傳播 , 一種利潤的動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採取了規則 , 減緩了創新 , 把中國從世界的其他地方砍掉 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 開發新規則 , 中國人也從這些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	在那裡的收入仍然不穩定 , 因為它在世界其他地方放大了 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	在中國 , 平均收入是美國平均所得的比例
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50年代和60年代 , 你們可以看到 , 大約佔了3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	經濟成長在中國起飛 , 中國開始迅速地接近美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖 , 就能得到一個線索 , 讓中國的規則有了巨大的改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的區域 , 各位可以看到 , 在外線的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 中國在二十世紀大部分的時間 , 運作在非常不同的規則下 , 比起當時工作市場經濟的其他中國規則 , 和英國的管理者 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個地方 , 在那裡 , 數百萬人可以去 , 從大陸 , 從工作開始 , 像是縫紉襯衫 , 玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了達到增加收入的過程 , 增加技能的進步 , 造成了非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 領導人 , 像丹尼烏托邦這樣的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定把所有大陸都搬到市場模型上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但匈牙利直覺地了解 , 對他的人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國所有人立即轉換到市場模式 , 他們採取了一些特殊區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的事:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要選擇的人可以選擇的 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們創造了四個特殊的經濟區塊 , 包含香港:區塊是中國人可以來工作的區塊 , 城市也在那裡快速成長 , 外國公司也可以進來 , 製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區塊有個城市叫 「 深圳 」 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在這個城市裡 , 有一個台灣公司 , 讓許多人擁有的iphone , 他們用中國人搬到那裡 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特別的區域之後 , 有14個沿海地區有著相同的開放性 , 最終在這些地方證明了成功 , 人們可以選擇的成功 , 因爲他們提供的好處 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功 , 導致了整個經濟體的市場模式前進的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的尺度上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變村落裡的規則 , 你就可以做到 , 但村落太小了 , 如果有數百萬人都在好的規則下工作 , 就能得到好處的好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給予一些人機會 , 看看事情是怎麼回事 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市能給你機會 , 創造出新的地方 , 新規則 , 讓人們能選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	他們夠大 , 能得到所有我們能擁有的好處 , 在好的規則下 , 數百萬人一起工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 我們的建議是 , 我們構想一個叫做 「 特區城市 」 的概念 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 來吸引我們需要建造城市的人們 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立起基礎建設──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、大樓 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 會僱用先搬到那邊的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 那些會來那裡住的居民 , 不久前會來 , 養育他們的孩子 , 接受教育給他們的孩子 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了這個章節 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以建設 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些是在文章中捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這其實是建立在模型中 , 如果我們能在未被居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	從未被人居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以活在新的章節之下 , 但沒有人被迫活在裡面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後 , 我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們希望領導人的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作夥伴有潛在的機會 , 實際上 , 德歐 , 中國和英國一起合作 , 首先建立一個小小的enclave的市場模式 , 然後擴大到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 無意間 , 透過香港的行動 , 讓世界貧窮減少了 , 比上個世紀 , 所有援助計畫都還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這類合作關係再複製它 , 我們就可以讓這類的益處在世界各地 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的程度 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的控制權 , 來克服某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這麼說時 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這是把殖民主義帶回來嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	這不是 。 但重要的是 , 要了解當我們開始思考這些事情時 , 會出現的那種情緒 , 會讓我們回去 , 可以關掉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義是不好的 , 在我們的援助計畫中 , 反而是它涉及了合作和保險的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇的 , 無論是領導者 , 還是對那些願意住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是對合作和保險的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	所以 , 咱們來談談這如何在實務上演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	我們拿一個特別的領導人 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領導人 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	它一定會發生在castro , 讓他有機會為古巴做些什麼 , 讓中國州長的 , 但他沒有香港在古巴島上 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他在南方有一點點光線 , 上面有非常特殊的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	那裡有一塊區域 , 位於古南達莫灣 , 在那裡 , 條約提供美國政府責任給一塊土地 , 大約曼哈頓兩倍大的土地 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去加拿大總理說: 「 看 , 伊恩克有個可怕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接管 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新城市在上面建設 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們在附近找香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的市民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會支持 , 但這將會是通往我的國家的通道 , 將現代經濟和現代世界連結起來的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模式還可以試試哪裡 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全得到一個特殊區塊的概念 , 讓人們可以當作規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方式 , 讓人們不需要合作 , 和合作的反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以做出更有信心的承諾 , 給長期投資者 , 來建造港口的投資者 , 建造道路 , 在一個新的城市裡 , 他們能做出更有信心的承諾 , 如果他們能和一個夥伴國家合作 , 他們就能做出更有信心的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在一些安排中 , 有點像escrow帳戶 , 把土地放進escrow帳戶中 , 合作的國家負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	在非洲 , 也有許多土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我飛往海岸時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	有著巨大的土地 , 像這樣的土地 , 數億人可以住在那裡 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個概念歸納起來 , 想想看 , 不僅僅有一兩個章節 , 還有數十個城市 , 能協助為數億人創造出地方 , 也許數十億人在未來的數十億人 , 他們會搬到城市裡 , 會有足夠的土地嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們晚上看著燈光 , 誤導的一件事 , 就是 , 視覺上 , 世界上大部分的燈都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我告訴各位 , 為什麼是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以所有土地的代表為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它轉換成一個正方形 , 代表著地球上所有可耕的土地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已被城市佔據的土地 , 三十億人口居住的城市 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形底下 , 你可以看到 , 現存的都市居民只佔地球上可耕地的3% 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們就會像這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從3%的可耕地 , 降到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大地減少地球上人類的足跡 , 藉由建造更多人能搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被好的規則所管理 , 他們可以成為城市 , 在那裡 , 人們是安全的 , 不受犯罪、疾病和不良的衛生限制 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們能取得基本的電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座章節城市 , 擴展它 , 這樣我們才能建造更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	可以用手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些細節 , 可以進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑出城市 , 走出去設計城市 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會在野外放學術界 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 假設它不僅僅是加拿大 , 還能處理拉爾卡斯壯的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也是 。 或許古巴想要成為一個合作夥伴 , 一個接收風險的四個合作夥伴 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有那麼早的預期 , 但很容易就成功了 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這一點 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時 , 土地的價值有巨大的收益 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付像警察、法院等東西 , 但學校和健康照護體系 , 讓這個地方更吸引人 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 發生了 , 讓土地變得更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 那些幫忙建構這個區塊的人的獎勵 , 建立了基本的規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有很多其他的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓低成本、負擔得起的建築 , 讓第一份工作的人 , 能夠組裝出像iphone一樣的東西 , 但要讓這些建築能節省能源 , 確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會掉在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節要被找出來 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些東西的人 , 已經知道沒有障礙 , 沒有障礙 , 除了想像的失敗之外 , 那會讓我們避免真正的全球雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	雖然地球上有這麼多人 , 我們之所以能做得很好 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享意味著我們減少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:管理我們如何互動的規則 , 例如 , 我們要有納稅系統 , 來支持一項研究大學 , 讓某些知識免費 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	我們要有一個系統 , 在一個政府辦公室裡 , 擁有土地的權利 , 人民可以承諾是殖民地 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 尤其是創新的 , 以改變規則的形式 , 我們就不會陷入不好的規則 , 那麼 , 我們就可以讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人和他的朋友不再需要在街燈下學習任何東西 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因學先驅克雷格•凡特在他史詩般的探險旅行中 , 休息了一段時間 , 來談談他的團隊發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 已經在它的追尋之中 , 以繪製海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物圈 , 生物科技 , 企業家 , 基因 , 發明 , 海洋 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 , 科技 ,
craig venter on dna and the sea	在dna和海洋上克雷格•凡特和克雷格•凡特 ,
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 有幾個人問我關於衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者遠比悲觀主義者還要活得多 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位的是 , 我們將如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換成第一階段 , 開始寫程式碼 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	直到十年前 , 這個月才發表了第一個免費生物的基因序列 , 大象流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年的基因組計畫 , 到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內做同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年間 , 許多基因組被加入了:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	在這個階段的基因組學 , 在十年前 , 到今年底 , 我們可能有三到五個基因序列 , 數百個基因組的序列 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金得到了獎金 , 今年我們將130種基因組定序為環保有機體的一副計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們觀察 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有把這個星球上可用的表面刮下來 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人都不知道 , 因為他們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成了地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物只組成了生物量的1/3 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許牛津的人們通常不會這麼做 , 但如果你把它們放到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 記住 , 每一毫升的海水中 , 大約有一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 只有不到五千種微生物種類的特徵 , 所以我們決定做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了索克er二世探險 , 在那裡 , 我們有著大量的海洋地理探險 , 試圖每200英哩的樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在百慕達做測試 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 下到美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越太平洋 , 跨越了印度洋的流程 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常困難的 , 我們在船隻上做這件事 , 部分原因是要協助刺激年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只用海水過濾 , 收集不同過濾器的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們可以每24小時將一億個基因編碼的基因編碼定序列 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	藉由這麼做 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 它認為我們眼中的視覺色素 , 環境中只有一到兩種有機體 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上所有海洋上層的物種 , 都擁有同樣的攝影器 , 使用陽光作為它們的能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和大約5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	現在我們將它延伸到空氣中 , 帶著來自losan基金會的補助金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量了有多少病毒和細菌每天都在呼吸中 , 尤其是在飛機上或關閉室內 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的表面過濾 , 我們收集了十億微生物 , 從紐約市的一座建築物上過濾出來 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正在進行定序的過程 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在數據集合的一面 , 就在加拉巴哥群島 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋中的樣本中就看到了巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些邏輯是合理的 , 以不同的溫度來說 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度紅色 , 很溫暖 , 很溫暖 , 很冷 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和寒冷的水樣本之間有很大的不同 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人驚訝的事 , 就是這些光感應器能偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的胺基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些區塊不同的地方 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	可能不意外 , 在深海 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 攝影師通常會看到藍色的光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠色的光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能更加不同 , 在極端的紅外線和紫外線運動 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	試試看看我們的基因複製品的評估 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 都來自探險 , 這代表了地球上所有基因資料的一半 , 總共有2億9百萬個基因基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因家庭放入基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是在發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但我們在環境中所採集的每一個新樣本 , 加上線性時尚 , 給這些新族群 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於這個星球上最早的發現基礎基因、元件和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的進化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物的角落 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組中 , 只有兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合在一起 , 我們大概有不到三萬人 , 可能有十幾種不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計成份 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為 , 在一個基因中心的觀點中 , 可能回到理查•達金斯的觀點 , 比基因組成的觀點 , 這觀點不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 已經改變了 , dna序列在過去的十年或二十年間 , dna序列的速度越來越快 , 便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們首先想到合成基因組學 , 是在1995年我們將第二種基因組定序後 , 這從我的生殖器中 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器材 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	大象有18000個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800個 , 另外500個物種 , 是否有一小組基因組組成一個最小的營運系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做交通突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉換器只是一小片dna , 隨機插入基因密碼中 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們在基因的中間插入 , 它們會破壞它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一份地圖 , 可以將轉換器插入的基因地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 不必要的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對於這個議題來說是很重要的 , 而你只能根據環境的特性來定義一個必要的或不必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用更直接的智能方法和13個相關有機體的基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較這些基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因在所有133個有機體上都常見 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略一個細胞寄生蟲 , 池塘就會擴大一點 ; 當我們觀察核心的基因 , 大約是310種左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴張或收縮基因 , 取決於你的觀點 , 從500到400個基因到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是要建構一個人造染色體 , 裡面有那些基因 , 我們得要在一個以casette為基礎的時尚中做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片碎片中 , 合成正確的dna是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	漢姆.史密斯和克萊德.哈特森 , 我的同事開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一組五千年巴爾病毒 , 只有百分之百準確 , 用它的序列和生物學來合成 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 然後殺死了細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒 , 一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年之前就已經被製造出來了 , 但它只需要一個十三分之一的病毒活性 , 花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個軟體現在建立了自己的硬體 , 這就是生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到關心生物戰爭的議題上 , 我在參議院委員會之前就有了近期的證詞 , 美國政府已經設立了檢討這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要保持現實是很重要的 , 要和大家的想像力會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今的任何病毒都可以進行基因組定序 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就對伊波拉或天花的事物感到驚訝 , 但這生物體的dna沒有感染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因組 , dna本身就不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正的擔憂是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	僅有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 正努力創造生物戰事代理 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這個研究真的被剝奪了 , 未來的設計師病毒應該就沒有什麼活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內 , 單細胞有機體是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能在十年內 , 我們所擁有的真皮細胞都有可能 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在正在製造好幾十種不同的構造 , 因為我們能改變貓咪和基因進入人造染色體的基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把所有其他人都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一套相同的重新組合系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體中衍生出來的 , 細微佔領無線電的無線電 , 只要有三百萬種放射線 , 且不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發的12到24小時後 , 它的染色體就會重新組合起來 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種有機體在地球上無所不在 , 可能是因為我們所有的旅行都在外太空中存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一台玻璃製造商 , 經過了五十萬個輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 當微生物坐在海底時 , 變得更開心和更開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張照片的實際情況是這樣的:頂端顯示了一百七十萬種放射線的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的會分崩離析 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna自動重組了24小時 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真正令人驚訝的是 , 這些有機體能做到這一點 , 而我們可能有數千種 , 如果不是成千上萬種 , 在這個星球上 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合成後 , 第一步是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	我們認為合成細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 更是希望環境和社會問題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從第三種有機體中 , 我們序列的第三種有機體 , 甲烷 , 詹納西 , 它的溫度是沸騰的 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 所有的碳 , 都來自於它所捕捉到的環境 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 成千上萬種不同的生物住在二氧化碳的外層 , 還能捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油來做合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 從大氣中捕捉碳 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種有機體 , 生活在二氧化碳之外 , 我們用它作為減少水分的力量 , 來產生氫和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 有很多途徑可以被改造出代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一項重大的計畫 , 用挪威的雕像來捕捉和把甲烷從加油場轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之內 , 我認為有一個新領域叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些大量的基因排列組合 , 以及同性組合的組合 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可能有一百萬個不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同生物學 , 你在篩選螢幕上的選擇 , 不論你在篩選氫氣生產 , 或化學生產 , 或僅是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因的角色 , 就會很順利 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光照射中直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們認為 , 氧氣敏感的氫氣會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在組合細胞分解 , 酶會分解複雜糖分成簡單的糖和發酵 , 在同一個細胞中產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥的生產 , 已經在大型實驗室中使用微生物 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學性質比我們最好的化合物所能製造出的強度還要複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的改造物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源、環境的補救來源 , 也許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年宣佈了實驗的開端 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物醫學評論 , 來評論我們是否該嘗試和製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與了這個 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖把他們的文字當作法律書 , 他們無法在這些文字中找到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以這一定是沒關係的 。 唯一的關注是生物戰略的面向 , 但給了我們未來的實驗 , 為我們做這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在 , sloan基金會剛剛資助了一份多個機構的研究 , 針對這個研究 , 找出社會的風險和益處是什麼 , 以及像我一樣的科學團隊所使用的規則 , 例如我應該在這個領域中使用 , 我們正嘗試建立一個好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅 , 在生物恐怖主義方面 , 它們非常簡單 , 我們能設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 也許革命了開發中國家能做的事 , 並提供各種簡單的過程 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利浦.辛巴多說幸福和成功是根源於我們大部分人不認同的特質:我們對過去、現在和未來的追求方式 。 他建議我們在這個時代 , 作為一個第一步 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心靈、心理學、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普•辛巴多會開處方一個健康的處方 , 花時間 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的概念 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘 。 30秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	請安靜下來 , 安定下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大約是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一次 。

philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•辛巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 不要太願望了 , 請咬一點 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 一口 。 到底是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑 , 全是為了賺錢 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 後來 , 衝動 , 反思 , 現在 , 焦點和未來 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	被保證的美德會被獵殺到當時的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	十幾歲的女孩 , 她們主張性別缺陷和處女 , 直到婚姻 , 感謝妳的喬治布希──多數 , 60% , 她們在一年內被性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分的人都沒有使用生育控制 。
so much for promises .	承諾是如此 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 , 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會付出代價 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	會發生三分之二的孩子給誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在他們延遲了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華特•密歇爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 14年後 , 試著去了解那些孩子有什麼不同 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 反抗和孩子的孩子之間有著巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些拒絕分數250分的孩子 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很龐大 。 這就像一大堆不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到任何麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且堅決的 。 今天對我來說 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是將來的 , 而不是現在的 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動分成時間區 , 或分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動地做 , 無意識地做出來 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們不同文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育程度之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們會變得偏見 , 因為你會學會過度使用他們 , 並且低估其他人 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做一個決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有當下的情況 , 其他人在做什麼 , 你的感覺 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	那些人 , 當他們做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是無關緊要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去經歷過的這種狀況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 「 過時 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在什麼 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是關於未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來 」 , 他們的焦點在未來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想爭論的是 , 時間觀點的悖論 , 會影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你對這些偏見的時間觀點有所偏見 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種方法 。 有兩種方法可以做簡報 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被偽造 , 成為未來的兩種方式 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在 「 反正 」 或 「 負面 」 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	可以說是你把焦點放在人生的喜悅上 , 或說是現代主義者──不重要 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超乎尋常的未來:命名是生命起源於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出靈活性 , 轉換時間觀點 , 取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光呢 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度反覆思考 。 未來的高度調整 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	而在現代主義上 , 調節現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是低於負面和現代主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的暫時混合是你從過去的過時性中得到的 , 會讓你有根源 。 你將你的家人、身份和自我連結在一起 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你得到的就是翅膀 , 到新目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的喜悅主義得到的 , 是能量 , 來探索你自己 , 地方 , 人們 , 感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間 , 過度的看法 , 都比正面的更加負面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來對成功的犧牲是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時光 , 犧牲個人的絕望 。
