they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 , 影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活在工作、成就和控制中 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信這和一些ted的演講者有共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我有共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯ghet托長大 , 一個醫師家庭 , 每個人都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位未來的人 , 他走過頂端 , 犧牲了所有這些犧牲 , 因為老師干預了 , 讓我有了未來的傾向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等一下你會拿到兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 我把焦點放在解讀性上 , 所以 , 七十六歲時 , 我比以往更有生產力、更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們要把這個應用到許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 增進青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療創傷後壓力症候群 , 讓永續發展和保育 , 降低實體復健率 , 讓自殺傾向 , 改變家庭衝突的方式 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以 , 我想以結尾說:許多人生的謎題 , 都可以透過了解你的時間和他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在一百年後 , 有多少人的頭條新聞會重要 ? 1000年 ? kirkcitron的 「 長期新聞 」 計畫 , 不只現今都重要 , 還會產生數十年 , 甚至2010年 , 他在ted2010年時 , 發出頭條的頭條 , 有潛力可以塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球性議題 , 媒體 , 新聞 , 科學 , 科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 還有真實的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞上淹沒了 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是自閉症 , 每年就有350萬個新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	這只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來看 , 實際上有多少故事會影響到這些故事 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是由長期的基金會成立的 , 由tedsters所創立的 , 包括凱文凱爾和史都華特品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞 , 新聞可能在50或10 , 000年後才會出現 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過這個過濾器看新聞時 , 很多事都掉下來了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 為了從a.p.的上層故事 , 去年 , 這將在十年內發生嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這會在50或100年內產生影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那真是太酷了 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 去年的頂尖故事是經濟 , 我敢打賭 , 不久後 , 這種衰退將會是舊消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 未來可能有什麼樣的故事會造成什麼樣的改變 ?
well , let's take science .	咱們來談科學 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血液 , 修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 那天就已經來了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真正的蜜蜂毒液將基因送到大腦裡 , 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今 , 我們有六十億人正在吃飯 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國沒有基因改造的作物 , 就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾•蓋茨有十億人參考過農業研究 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界將會非常不一樣 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 他們也可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超越了美國 , 因為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超越德國成為最大的出口者 , 他們開始做dna測試 , 讓孩子選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法來推動我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	有些近期的發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每一個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自主導導向的機器人科學家 , 很快地 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命也不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後就被破壞了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 若沒有我們 , 生命就會持續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 去年 , 我挑選的最新新聞是這個:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群放在那裡比較容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能 , 或在座的某個人可能會寫一支大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	地球科學家卡羅琳•普拉科在卡西尼航行的照片上 , 展示了來自土星的影像 , 專注在它最大的衛星、土衛六上 , 以及凍土龍上 , 似乎是冰的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署 , 設計 , 探索 , 探索 , 科學 , 太空 , 太空 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡羅琳•普拉科讓我們飛到土星上 , 飛到土星上 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一個旅程 , 你和我已經經歷過很多年了 , 五十年前 , 當人類踏出地球時 , 它就開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅真的在月球上設定了腳 , 還把機械太空船分散到所有行星的八個行星上 , 我們已經降落在小行星上 , 我們已經把彗星重新生長了 , 在這個時點 , 我們有了一艘太空船 , 用它的方式 , 冥王星 , 身體前所知的行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類大型旅程的一部分:航海來了解事物 , 去了解宇宙的起源 , 去了解我們的起源 , 地球 , 和地球 , 我們的生活 , 來到這裡 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方 , 我們可能會去找尋像這樣的問題的答案 , 土星 , 在1980年代初期 , 我們已經去土星了 。 我們已經去過土星 , 但是我們在土星的調查之後 , 土星的調查已經變得更加深入 , 因為卡西尼號太空船 , 穿越了星際空間的旅行 , 在2004年的夏天 , 成為了人類最遙遠的飛行軌道機器人 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是有錢的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 顯然的 , 超越了比較 , 這項系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙範圍 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光靠研究環 , 我們就能學到很多關於星星和氣體的分散 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是andromedanebula的美麗照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡有一座美麗的螺旋槳星系是由哈伯望遠鏡所拍攝的 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程是真正的一部分 , 也是人類航海的一個比喻 , 來了解我們周遭的所有事物之間的關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入這張圖片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我無法告訴你們我們在卡西尼學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法給你們看我們過去兩年半所拍攝的所有美麗的照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我將專注在兩件最令人興奮的故事中 , 其中有兩件最令人興奮的故事 , 發生在這個重大的探索探險旅程中 , 我們正在進行土星四周進行的探險旅程 , 過去兩年半 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星是由非常大且多樣化的衛星所組成的 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里跨越到美國的大小 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們拍攝了土星的美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星與它的衛星有一些月球 , 這是土星的土星 , 土星是鑽石 , 然後是土星 , 這是土星的土星 , 這裡是土衛二 , 向你展示了它們的垂直薄度 , 和土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	土星的47顆衛星中有兩個是標準的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼到達那裡之前 , 最大的一個未被探索的地帶 , 是我們的太陽系中仍有的 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這種身體長久以來都對觀察行星的人感到很有興趣 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常大 , 厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像我們在地球上所居住的環境 , 至少在過去 , 是太陽系中任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮氣 , 就像你在這房間呼吸一樣 , 只是它的大氣層充滿了簡單的有機物質 , 例如甲烷、甲烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在泰坦大氣層的高空中會被打破 , 而它們的產品會結合在一起 , 製造毛髮粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個消費者是無所不在的 。 它是全球性的 , 並且加入titan 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這就是為什麼你看不見我們眼睛的表面在可見光譜的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀粒子 , 在我們和卡西尼到達之前 , 經過數十億年的時間 , 溫和地表覆蓋在厚厚的有機煙霧中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像等同 , 等同於泰坦、焦油、石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們懷疑的 。 這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 在泰坦的表面溫度上 , 可能是液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要把水送到地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	在大氣層中 , 它是可被保密的 , 所以 , 認知了這個環境 , 帶來了整個奇異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在這些雲層之上 , 你有數百公里的海底 , 這樣就能防止任何陽光從表面照射到表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管如此寒冷 , 泰坦的表面下下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上下雨是怎麼回事:它會雕刻出水底 , 形成河流和水泥 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石坑中聚集 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以洗掉高山頂和山丘 , 下到低地 , 停下來 , 想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像泰坦的表面是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 在泰坦 , 高處就跟地球上深處的地球光線一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很冷 , 很天真 , 很糟糕 , 可能是下雨 , 你可能站在密西根湖的岸邊 , 用油漆薄的薄荷來模仿 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號和泰坦的表面之前所看到的景象 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在泰坦所發現的 , 雖然它的細節不一樣 , 都和故事一樣令人著迷 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼人一樣 , 就像是青少年凡爾冒險一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有厚厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這張照片是titan , 來自太陽的背景 , 背景是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個衛星 , 我甚至不知道它是哪一個 。 它是大氣層非常大的一部分 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號的工具 , 可以透過這個大氣層看到海面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 就跟我們差不多那樣 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們不能在泰坦看到什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域時 , 你就會開始看到像我們不知道的無數頻道一樣的東西 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面有非常少的隕石坑 , 意思是它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來很像地質 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你在行星上看到線條時 , 就意味著有一個裂痕 , 例如一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經有了直升的變化 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但 , 我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件事件 , 許多人都被視為卡西尼的調查的高度調查 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是huygens探測器的部署 , 歐洲的builthuygens探測器 , 卡西尼已經在太陽系中運行了七年 。 我們將它部署到titan的大氣層 , 花了2.5小時 , 下降了地表 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我想強調一下這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在人類史上第一次在外太陽系內降落 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	顯而易見的是 , 在我心目中 , 這事件應該被讚頌 , 在美國和歐洲的每個城市中 , 都應該有精彩的膠帶遊行 , 可悲的是 , 這不是事實 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很重要 , 因為有另一個原因 。 這是國際的使命 , 這事件在歐洲、德國被讚頌 , 而慶祝的英語和美國口音 , 和德國的口音 , 德國的口音 , 法國人和義大利人和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	它是關於 「 聯合國 」 所謂的 「 聯合國 」 的演示 , 應該是意義:一個真正的國家團結在一起 , 為了好的 , 共同努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 要去探索一個行星 , 要了解一個行星系統 , 在所有人類歷史上 , 都無法做到 , 現在 , 人類已經碰到它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我會去吃雞皮疙瘩 , 去談它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不應該 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	無論如何 , 探測器在下面測量大氣層的測量結果也拍了全景照片
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器表面的第一張圖片看到泰坦的表面 。 這是我們看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是件令人震驚的事 , 因為我們希望這些照片從軌道上拍攝的所有其他照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	它是一個不明確的圖案 , 地質圖案 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這是一種只由液體流動而形成的趨勢的趨勢 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以追蹤這些頻道 , 你可以看到它們如何混合在一起 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們聚集在這個頻道上 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍攝的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好吧 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里 , 這大約是航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你會在高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在泰坦航空的窗口 , 飛越過泰坦的表面 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在表面上留下休息 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系的表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰塊 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它降落在這些平坦的黑暗區域中 , 它並沒有從視覺中沉下來 。 所以它不是我們降落的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器下到的基本上等同於泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一片無解的土地 , 裡面有液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種材料已經在我們看到的這些通道上被洗掉了數十億年的土地 , 填滿了低含水池的土地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是幽默探測器降落的樣子 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 我們的影像中沒有標誌 , 甚至在huygens的影像中 , 沒有任何大型的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 情況更加令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們的titan赤道區域的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高達100公尺高 , 分開了幾公里 , 它們延伸了幾英里 , 甚至幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百人 , 高達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是撒哈拉沙漠泰坦 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次地 , 它的謎題是 , 沒有液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了北極區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在泰坦南極的南極區 , 有一個湖景 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約是安大略湖的大小
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 一週半前 , 我們飛越了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們發現了一顆特徵 , 大小和加勒比亞海一樣大 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎我們不明白的原因 , 基於某些我們不明白的原因 , 至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地 , 泰坦的北極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們會同意 , 我們找到泰坦是個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它是外星人 , 但它是外星人 , 但很奇怪的地球 , 且有著像地球般的地質組成 , 和一個巨大的地理多樣性 , 一個令人著迷的世界 , 世界上只有太陽系的複雜性 , 豐富本身才是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	現在我們進入土衛二.土衛二是一個小的衛星 , 大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它在英格蘭旁邊 , 展示它的大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二非常白 , 非常亮 , 它的表面顯然是碎裂 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質上活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二的媽媽在南極找到了新發現 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 我們發現了這個破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的組合 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們是編碼的 。 這些折斷是用有機材料編碼的 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個區域 , 南極的區域 , 已經升高了溫度 。 它是地球上最熱的地方 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這相當奇怪 , 發現地球上南極的溫度比熱帶的熱量還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們拍了額外的圖片時 , 我們發現 , 從這些碎片中 , 正是發射出精細的噴射機 , 冰粒會延伸上數百英里的空間 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們顏色編碼這張圖片時 , 要把微弱的光線帶出來 , 我們看到這些噴射機在其他的影像中 , 在土衛二上方數千英里 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我的團隊和我已經檢查過像這樣的圖片 , 像這張圖片 , 考慮到在卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射機可能在土衛二的表面下噴出液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能有液態水、有機材料和過多的熱能 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們很有可能發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個可能適合活生生生的有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中其他地方 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學暗示 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明遺傳的數量不曾發生過 , 但在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立兩次 , 那就表示 , 根據推斷 , 它在整個宇宙中發生了很驚人的數量 , 且它的歷史有137億年 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍然是唯一一個我們所知的行星 , 正與生命結合在一起 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 只有我們所知的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們在1960年代時期有任何人在警告和合作 , 原諒你 , 如果你不是 , 那麼你會記得1968年阿波羅8號著名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是地球第一次來自太空 , 地球對我們在宇宙中所處的感受有著巨大的衝擊 , 我們對地球的保護有責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	首先 , 我們在卡西尼拍了一張相同的照片 , 一張人類從未見過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全食 , 從土星的另一側看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個美麗的圖片中 , 你看到的是太陽的主要環 , 你看到的是太陽的反射影像 , 你可以看到這個環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的散射出去 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們就可以看到 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的手臂上被撞上了 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一個非常深刻的動作 , 就是要從afar看到自己 , 捕捉到我們在其他世界的小藍綠色的星球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	我們從中得到的這個觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到最棒的獎勵 , 開始了半個世紀 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人口被繪製出來 。 這張地圖在災難之後 , 提供了援助 , 隱藏了土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這短短篇的演講中 , 谷歌的拉特•卡•加德莫達所繪製的地圖 , 一個團體地圖描繪了全世界的人所使用的地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 技術 , 技術 , 合作 ,
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近的katradagda:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體系 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	在2008年 , 颶風納格斯•納格斯瓦解了巨大的緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人非常需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人民和供給壓在這個地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法協助到達自行車受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被描繪成可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國在解決世界上絕大多數多面孔的問題:沒有細節的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40位志工用了一套新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路 , 三千間醫院 , 物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? 谷歌地圖工人 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	谷歌地圖製造者是一項技術 , 讓我們每個人都能繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用了這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 影片商店到角落 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名赫南多德•索托托發現 , 大部分開發中國家的經濟專利的關鍵在於要採用大量未被開發的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 單單在印度 , 就有一兆美元的房地產 , 仍然沒有被開發出來 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 在170個國家 , 就有數千名使用者繪製了數百萬個資訊 , 創造出了一幅地圖 , 不可思議的地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這讓熱情使用者的力量無所不在 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	咱們來看看一些使用者的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 如我們所說的 , 在這170個國家 , 人們在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家很近 , 在班加羅爾一個n.g.路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機幾何學的結果 , 手勢識別 , 機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數百個城市中數千個使用者的勝利 , 一個使用者 , 一次一次編輯一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未被應用的星球70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 布德魯的巴勒斯坦村子登上了十個月大的非暴力抗議活動 , 阻止在他們橄欖的墳墓中建造障礙 。 你有聽說過嗎 ? 巴西的電影製作者茱莉亞問為什麼我們只關注在以色列史上最衝突的暴力事件 , 而非暴力的領導者 , 有一天可能會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情心、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱利亞•巴赫亞:請注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總是有一個問題出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了數十個巴勒斯坦人拍攝了非暴力行為 , 用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者試圖忘記一項巨大的全國非暴力運動 , 終結該地區的職業 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 你們大部分人可能從來沒有聽過他們說過 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	在這地面上和國外的感知之間的分歧就是為什麼我們還沒有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	今天我在這裡要談的是注意力 , 關注力的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩和其他地方的非暴力運動 , 及發展的力量 , 今天 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 非暴力成長的主要原因不是巴勒斯坦人要開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經存在的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明一下這個點 , 把你們帶到這個叫布德魯斯的村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨滅絕 , 因為以色列宣布要建造一個隔離障礙 , 其中一部分的障礙是建在村子上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去百分之四十的土地 , 被包圍 , 所以他們會失去西岸的免費權 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發起了一項和平的抗爭活動 , 來阻止這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你看一些短片 , 所以你對於那些在地面上看起來是什麼樣子的感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知 , 牆壁將巴勒斯坦與以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現牆會偷竊我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男人:柵欄事實上 , 創造出了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去和平遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被幾十位以色列兄弟和姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列的行動主義者:沒有比非暴力的反對者更害怕軍隊 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們都做不到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔•派對會員:我們必須清空傳統思維的思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想要傳播給所有的巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔 , 哈馬斯和流行的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:圍籬持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們可以使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是活生的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就像是低音jah , 到處拍攝 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列的行動主義者:我相信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人 , 甚至沒有牛奶 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止它 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是一個和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	沒有需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們可以做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱利亞•巴契亞:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體並沒有報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過了10個月的和平抗爭之後 , 說服了以色列政府把障礙從他們的土地和綠色的路線 , 也就是國際認可的以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德魯斯的抗藥性已經傳播到西岸的村莊 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默對非暴力的可能性造成了深遠的後果 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭對手共有非常重要的一件事 , 他們都是舞台尋找觀眾的形式 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷地被封鎖 , 吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題 , 這對非暴力的領導者來說 , 對他們的社區來說 , 民間失能是可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量 , 可能會對房間裡的父母來說是毫無意外的 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子變得越來越大聲 , 最肯定的方法就是讓他注意到他第一次投擲一個符號 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	幻肢會變成兒時心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道他能從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以獎勵或不獎勵的行為 , 只要給予孩子或吸引孩子的注意 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 取決於國際社群選擇關注的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 要結束中東衝突的核心 , 帶給和平的核心 , 就是要把非暴力行為轉變成一個功能性行為 , 讓我們能更加關注現今的非暴力領袖 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝我的電影的過程中 , 在西岸、加薩、東耶路撒冷 , 我看到 , 甚至一部紀錄片都有可能會影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉je的村莊裡 , 這座村莊很接近耶路撒冷 , 社區正面臨著和布德魯斯非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 損失很多土地 , 沒有自由取得 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力暴力 , 但從沒人在注意到他們之後 , 他們就被剝削了 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們組織了一個螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好的示範 , 展現到目前為止 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德魯斯的故事 , 在電影中被記錄下來 , 感覺到 , 確實有人遵守他們在做的事 , 人們關心這件事 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列 , 有一個新的和平運動 , 叫做索利達里特 , 意思是希伯來文的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領導者 , 一直在使用布德魯斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們說 , 以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	華拉吉和索利達里特運動的例子 , 顯示即使是小型的預算獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力變成功能行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導周圍的非暴力演示 , 在村莊裡發生 , 例如巴爾的尼爾、尼恩的 , 瓦拉耶 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰坊 , 如夏克•傑拉和斯•史爾瓦 , 非暴力領導人會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像它們從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我已經見識過如果我們這麼做 , 他們會互相乘載 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果它們相乘的話 , 它們的影響會在以色列的巴勒斯坦衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於解開了情況 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導者證實了非暴力行為在布德魯斯之類的地方 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	把注意力給他們 , 讓他們可以在各處證明它是可行的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙尼克有一個簡單但有影響力的模式 , 以鼓舞人心的領導階層 , 都從金色圈開始 , 問: 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullsey , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 成功 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	賽蒙.辛克:偉大的領導人如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所想的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠做到一些事情 , 那些似乎無法打敗所有假設時 , 你要如何解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都還要有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有相同的才能 , 相同的機構 , 相同的顧問 , 相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼為什麼他們似乎有不同的東西呢 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩領導了民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受苦的人 , 他肯定不是白天唯一的偉大演說者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠找出控制權力的人飛機 , 當時還有其他更好的資金、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成動力的飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了飛機 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有別的 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一項發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這項發現深深地改變了我對世界運作的方式的看法 , 它甚至徹底改變了我對世界運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有的偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 或他們都認為的萊特兄弟 , 都一樣 , 行為和溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我做的就是編寫它 , 可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為 「 黃金圈 」 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 為什麼 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這一點點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠啟發其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	地球上每一個人 , 每一個組織都知道自己在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不管你稱它為你不同的價值觀 , 或你的財產過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但非常非常非常少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做他們要做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	根據 「 為什麼 」 , 我不是要 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	根據 「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的原因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	你為什麼要早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們思考的方式 , 我們溝通的方式 , 是從外面來的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 , 我們從最清晰的事物到最令人困惑的事物 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但這些啟發的領導者和靈感的組織 , 不論他們的大小 , 不論他們的產業都認為 , 行為和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果是因為他們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們的設計很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用和使用者 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」 「 啊 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷是這樣做的 , 大部分的銷售量是這樣做的 , 這也是大部分人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說我們所做的事 , 我們會說我們是不同的 , 或我們如何表現得更好 , 期待某種行為 , 購買 , 投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為我們的客戶表演 , 和我們合作的客戶 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的氣體 , 它有皮革座位 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現況的方式是 , 把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 簡單地使用和使用者 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好能製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是逆轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼要做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都很舒服從蘋果購買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒服從蘋果購買mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區別他們的競爭者的結構性 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同等資格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 大門發佈了平面螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們非常有資格製作平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在做平面螢幕監測器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	dell帶著mp3球員和pdas一起出發 , 他們生產了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計 , 沒有人買的產品 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在 , 談到這件事 , 我們甚至無法想像購買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	你為什麼要從電腦公司購買mp3球員 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你的東西做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和那些相信你所相信的人們做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我要告訴你們的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	一切都基於生物學的10個基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看看人類大腦的交叉處 , 從下面向下看 , 你會發現 , 人類的大腦其實被分成三種主要的元件 , 完美地和黃金圈連結在一起 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 和 「 什麼 」 等級相對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮層負責所有的理性、分析思考和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成了我們的肢體大腦 , 我們的肢體大腦負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	對於所有人類行為 , 所有決策 , 都沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 比如特徵、好處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它只是不動作 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們從內部溝通時 , 我們會直接對話到控制行為的大腦部位 , 然後我們允許人們將它合理化 , 用我們說和做的事 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道的 , 有時候你會給別人所有事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但這感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 沒有 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為大腦控制決策的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	最好的一點是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你會說你是帶著你的心 , 或者你是帶著你的靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭打破它 , 不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的肢體大腦中 , 大腦控制決策 , 而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你做你做的事 , 人們會回應為什麼你做你做的事 , 那麼你會如何讓人們投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 想要成為你做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給那些需要你的東西的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們 , 只因為他們可以做工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你僱用那些相信你所相信的人們 , 他們會用血汗和淚水來工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他地方比萊特兄弟更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求權力飛行的追求 , 就像白天的網際網路一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley所擁有的 , 我們所假設的 , 是成功的配方 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我是說 , 即使是現在 , 你問大家: 「 你的產品為什麼會這樣 ? 公司為什麼會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的三件事:被低估、錯誤的人、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	永遠都是相同的三件事 , 咱們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley得到了五萬美金的戰爭部門 , 想出這台飛行器 。
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一座座座椅 , 在史密森尼亞人工作 , 非常有連結性 ; 他知道白天的所有思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用最好的心智資金 , 找到最好的資金 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報到處都跟著他 , 每個人都在為langley的根源 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里外 , 在俄亥俄州 , 奧維爾和威爾布萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的配方 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 帶著自行車店的成果 ; 在萊特兄弟的團隊中 , 沒有一個人擁有大學教育 , 甚至沒有邪惡 , 甚至是牛羚 ; 紐約時報都跟著他們到處走 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 奧維爾和威爾布爾是由一個理想所驅動的 , 由一個目的 , 一個信念驅動的 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能弄清楚飛行器 , 就會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 而且他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想 , 與他們合作 , 血汗和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另外一些人才剛為付錢工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是 , 每次萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們就要服用五套零件 , 因為這是他們在供應商之前會墜機幾次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟搭飛機 , 沒有人能體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證據證明拉格利的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟搭飛機的那天 , 他辭掉了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 那真是很了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一個 , 他沒有富有 , 他沒有出名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的事物 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的事物的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的那些人 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的 「 創新定律 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的直播者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的多數人 , 你的多數人 , 和你的缺點 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人購買觸覺電話的唯一原因是你再也買不起新式手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	在這個規模上 , 我們都坐在不同時間點 , 但創新的傳播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受這個點子 , 你無法做到 , 直到你達到15%到18%之間的市場入侵點 , 然後系統尖端 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 大約10% 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人只是 「 取得它 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們描述他們的方式 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那種直覺的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們只是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到那些在你和他們做生意之前得到的資訊 , 和那些不懂的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 這裡的這個小差距 , 如同jefffreymoore所說的 , 「 交叉迷宮 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期的大多數都不會嘗試 , 直到有人先試過它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些傢伙 , 創新者 , 早期的採用者 , 他們很舒服地做出這些腸道決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更加自在地做出那些由他們對世界的信念所驅動的直覺決策 , 而不僅僅是產品的可用性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊六個小時買iphone , 當他們出櫃時 , 只要你走進店裡 , 買了一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面螢幕電視上 , 當他們出櫃時 , 即便科技是次級的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己做到了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	那是因為他們想要成為第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 以及你所做的 , 證明了你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做一些事情來證明他們所相信的 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	在前六個小時內 , 買了iphone的原因 , 站在那條線上 , 六個小時 , 是因為他們對這個世界的信念 , 以及他們想要大家看的是什麼:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗和一個著名的創新定律 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們先前所說的 , 第二年前 , 成功的食譜是金錢 , 正確的人和正確的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo出版大約八、九年前到今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金非常高 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo作為動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是在垃圾時間華納dvr上綁東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們到ipo時 , 他們的股價大約是30或40美元 , 再下跌 , 也從來沒有超過10美元的交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它在六號以上的交易 , 除了幾個小尖刺 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你知道 , 當tivo發表他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們所有的產品 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一台能暫停現場電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 重新播放現場電視 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 不用問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全控制你人生的各個面向的人 , 男孩 , 我們有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它停止了現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的就是證明你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在 , 讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明了創新法律的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人在華盛頓的購物中心出現 , 聽見金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有發送邀請 , 沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	你要怎麼做 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個受過公民權威的美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子不好 。
but he had a gift .	但他有個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有四處告訴人們 , 美國需要什麼才能改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	相信他所相信的成因的人 , 讓他自己成立 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人發出這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	各位 , 在右一天 , 有25萬人在對的日子 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席了 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己而出 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們相信的美國 , 讓他們在巴士旅行了八個小時 , 讓他們站在華盛頓中期 , 站在華盛頓 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種法律:那些由高權威所製成的法律 , 以及由人類所製成的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類所製成的法律 , 都與較高權威制度所制定的法律一致 , 直到我們生活在一個公平的世界中 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好發生了 , 民權運動是幫助他帶來生命的完美目標 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟著 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在 , 聽聽政治人物 , 他們全面的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有啟發任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者擁有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導者卻啟發了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們會跟隨那些領導者 , 不是因為我們需要 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟著那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 他們有能力啟發他們周圍的人 , 或找到啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你把車停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道如果你在正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家neilburges研究了我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學、科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 ?
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大停車場停車時 , 我們要如何記得我們停車在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是荷馬所面臨的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦裡發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬迴開始 , 在黃色的黃色部分 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損害 , 就像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你無法記住東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是用拉丁文命名為 「 海馬 」 , 它是相似的 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人類的大腦中大約有一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相溝通 , 透過發送小脈衝 , 或發電互相連結 , 彼此溝通 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬迴是由兩組細胞組成 , 非常緊密的相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元 , 或老鼠的記錄 , 來探索環境尋找食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們正在記錄這隻老鼠的海馬體中的一個單一神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發電時 , 就會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到這個神經元知道 , 當老鼠進入一個特定的環境時 , 老鼠就會知道這個特定的位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它會發出訊號到大腦的其他部位 , 只要發送一點電刺激 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以 , 我們可以把神經元的激發速度當作動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物在環境的不同部位移動時 , 不同的神經元會發出訊號 , 就像這個正方形的盒子 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起成立了一張對大腦的地圖 , 不斷地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	在人體中 , 位置細胞也會被記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時會需要大腦監控的電子活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩了個電玩遊戲 , 開車到一個小鎮上 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬迴中的細胞會被激發 , 當它們開車經過一個特定的小鎮時 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個地方細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人的環境中有哪些地方 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上層的人喜歡在老鼠的盒子的牆壁之間開火 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴展盒子時 , 激發的地點會膨脹 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面有一道火災 , 每當有一道牆在南邊時 , 都很喜歡開火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞會在兩個地方開火 , 不論在哪裡有一面牆 , 到南方 , 當動物在盒子裡探索時 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測預測 , 在你周圍建築物的邊界和方向 , 對於海馬體而言 , 尤其重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬迴的輸入中 , 細胞會發現海馬迴的專案計畫 , 會完全反應出邊界或邊緣 , 特別是從老鼠身上或老鼠身上 , 或老鼠身上的方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近一面牆時 , 就會開火 , 不論是邊緣或邊緣 , 或邊緣 , 不論是方框或圓形牆壁 , 或甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物都在邊緣 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發酵 , 當南邊有邊界時 , 不論是桌邊的邊緣 , 或牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 這就是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在四處探索的哪些地方 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物品的位置 , 像是這個目標旗 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 通常它們很擅長把標記在他們認為旗幟或車的位置上 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們用安置細胞做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟在哪裡 , 隨著環境的形狀和大小的改變 , 改變了你對環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你看到旗幟在一個小方形的環境中交叉 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 你就會把環境變得更大 , 他們認為旗幟已經被延伸出去了 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記得旗幟在你所有位置的位置中 , 藉由儲存在你所有位置的位置 , 然後你就可以回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以最符合你所在的位置細胞激發出的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這引導你回到你想要記得的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在運動的哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們採取一些出乎意料的路徑 , 或許我們停在公園之外 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的運動 , 可以整理這條路 , 大約是頭部方向的回路 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也能從一種稱為網格細胞的細胞中得到這種整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞再次被發現 , 輸入到海馬體上 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個單獨的細胞會在一系列不同的地點上發出一系列的不同位置 , 在一個驚人的三角形網格中 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從數個網格細胞中記錄下來 , 顯示在不同顏色的不同顏色中 , 每個細胞發射的格狀圖案會稍微轉移到其他細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的則在這個格子上發出綠色的 , 在這張圖上 , 藍色的 , 在這張 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 同心協力 , 老鼠可以在周圍環境中放上虛擬網格 , 有點像你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動時 , 電子活動可以從其中一個細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的運動 , 知道它在環境中位置的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有像格狀的發射模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的網格 , 在橘色中顯示 , 這意味著 , 網格細胞的活動 , 在特定的部分 , 大腦中 , 都應該根據六個方向進行改變 , 或在六個方向進行跑步 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人放進磁共振掃描儀 , 讓他們做個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我給你們看的一樣 , 尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人體皮質中看到的 , 和老鼠身上看到的網格細胞一樣 。
so back to homer .	回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他車子的位置 , 距離和方向的位置 , 可以延伸建築和界限 , 讓他停在地點 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	藉由激發偵測細胞的激發來來表示 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他走出車公園的路徑 , 可以用格子細胞的激發性來表示 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞開火 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他停在停車位的位置 , 這樣他就可以找到最好的位置 , 最符合大腦中位置細胞的發射模式 , 目前他將車停在位置的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到不尊重視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被破壞了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去抓它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶以外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這個網格發射的圖案 , 我們在一系列的位置中看到它 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是會活躍的 , 比如 , 記得你上次到婚禮時的記憶 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 也許 , 代表我們周遭空間的神經機制也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就可以重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們時 , 發生在我們身上的事件中 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果發生了這一切 , 你的記憶可以從細胞開始 , 藉由這些密集的連接 , 然後反應邊際細胞 , 創造出周圍景的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們會像對你面對的方向一樣開火 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看的方向 , 從你想要為你的視覺影像產生一張影像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮時 , 發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理學的過程 , 例如你如何記住或想像 , 甚至是以數十億個獨立的神經元的形式來思考 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾合作所驅動的 , 這不僅僅是開放資源的粉絲的遠端希望 , 而是詹姆斯•史塔維迪迪迪 , 最高層的nato總統委員會 , 他分享了來自近期的軍事史 , 來解釋為什麼未來的安全應該要用橋樑建造 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開源、和平、政治、社群媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯.斯特瓦里迪斯:娜托的最高指揮家如何看待全球安全管理局 , 如何看待全球安全局 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我打算談開放資源的安全性 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須要更好 。
